Life of Imam al-Ashari
beginner
5 min
Imam Ash'ari's Role: Reaffirming the Salaf's Creed
Editorial introduction defending al-Ash'ari's methodology and rejecting the claim he founded a new school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam al-Ash'ari did not invent a new creed but rather defended and systematically articulated the creed of the Salaf, harmonizing revelation and reason.

Core Idea
Imam al-Ash'ari reaffirmed the Salaf's creed; he did not found a new madhhab.

This passage from the introduction to an edition of an Ash'ari text clarifies a fundamental misunderstanding about Imam al-Ash'ari. Many assume he created a new theological school after leaving the Mu'tazila. The author argues that al-Ash'ari's work was a restatement of the Salaf's faith, using rational methods to reveal its harmony with reason. As you read, note how the author defends this view using historical evidence and a quote from a later scholar.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
The Arabic uses a formal academic style; don't worry about every word initially.
2
Identify the central argument
The author is refuting the claim that al-Ash'ari founded a new madhhab. Locate where he states the correct view and note the key phrase 'presented a new presentation of the creeds of the Salaf'.
Contrast the two positions: 'new madhhab' vs. 'new presentation of Salaf's creeds'.
3
Analyze the quote from al-Subki
Read the quote from Imam Taj al-Din al-Subki carefully. He uses two negations and one affirmation. Identify what al-Ash'ari did NOT do and what he DID do.
Al-Subki's statement is a concise summary of the passage's main point.
4
Reflect on the method of harmony
The passage emphasizes that al-Ash'ari's method revealed the harmony between revelation and reason. Think about why this was needed against both extreme textualists and the Mu'tazila.
This harmony is a key contribution of al-Ash'ari to Islamic thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأمرُ الثاني الذي حملني على التردد في تقدمة هذا التحقيق العلميّ لأقدم نص من نصوص المذهب الأشعري : ما أعلَمُه من عمق تراث الإمام الأشعري وسَعَتِه، وكثرة تصانيفه وتآليفه، وتعدُّدِ مجالاتها وتوزُّعها على كل موضوعات العلوم والمعارفِ السائدة في عصره، وبخاصة : علم الكلام [ علم العقيدة] الذي حَظِي على يديه بما يشبه ثورة تصحيح لكل الاضطرابات التي كان يعاني منها الفكر الإسلامي في ذلك الوقتِ، وبخاصة في علوم العقيدة: أصولاً وفروعًا، والتي كادت أن تنحرف بالعقل الإسلامي انحرافا خطيرًا، وبعيدا عما قرَّره القرآن الكريمُ، والسُّنَّة النبوية، وسلفُ الأُمَّةِ، في العقيدة والشريعة وعَلاقة الإنسانِ بالله وبالعالم، سواء على يد المعتزلة أو يد غُلاة النَّصَّيِّين. ومَن يقرأ كتاب مجرَّد مقالات الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري»، أو يستعرض فهرس مسائله، التي كان للإمام في كل مسألة منها موقف نقدي دقيق - يدرك إحاطة هذا الإمام بمعارفِ عصره وعلومه، وتقييمها والحكم لها أو عليها في ضوء خلفية علمية ثابتة يمكن تلخيصها في كلمة واحدة هي: «ما كان عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وصحابته وسلف الأمة» . ولعل هذا ما يفسر لنا رفض كثيرين من أئمة الكلام» أن يُقال عن الإمام الأشعري» : إنَّه بعد أن تحرَّرَ من ربقة المعتزلة طالَعَ الناسَ بمذهب جديد في العقائد والصحيحُ : أنه طالعهم بعرض جديد لعقائد السَّلف، وبمنهج جديد أيضًا كشف فيه الاتساق الكامل، في الواقع ونفس الأمر بين النقل والعقل، والذي عجز عن كشفه هؤلاء الذين أشرنا إليهم من غُلاة النَّصَّيِّين مِمَّن ثَقُل عليهم النظرُ العقلي ، والمعتزلة وسائرِ الفِرَقِ الأخرى . يقول الإمام تاج الدين السبكي : اعلم أنَّ الأشعري «لم يُبدع رأيًا ولم يُنشئ مذهبًا، وإنما هو مقرّر لمذاهبِ السَّلفِ مُناضِلٌ عما كانت عليه صحابه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فالانتساب إليه باعتبار أنه تَمَسَّك بذلك
The second matter that caused me to hesitate in presenting this scientific edition of the oldest text of the Ash'ari school: what I know of the depth of Imam al-Ash'ari's legacy and its breadth, the abundance of his writings and works, the diversity of their fields and their distribution over all topics of the sciences and knowledge prevalent in his time, especially the science of kalam (the science of creed), which gained at his hands something resembling a revolution of correction for all the disorders from which Islamic thought was suffering at that time, especially in the sciences of creed: fundamentals and branches, which nearly deviated the Islamic mind in a dangerous deviation, far from what the noble Qur'an, the Prophetic Sunnah, and the Salaf of the Ummah had established in creed, law, and the relationship of man with God and the world, whether at the hands of the Mu'tazila or the hands of the extreme textualists. Whoever reads the book 'Maqalat al-Shaykh Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' or reviews the index of its issues, in each of which the Imam had a precise critical position, realizes this Imam's encompassing knowledge of the sciences of his time, and his evaluation and judgment for or against them in light of a fixed scientific background that can be summarized in one phrase: 'What the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, his Companions, and the Salaf of the Ummah were upon.' Perhaps this explains to us the refusal of many of the imams of kalam that it be said about Imam al-Ash'ari that after he freed himself from the bondage of the Mu'tazila, he presented to the people a new madhhab in creeds. The correct view is that he presented to them a new presentation of the creeds of the Salaf, and with a new method that revealed the complete harmony, in reality and in the very matter, between transmitted revelation and reason, which those we referred to—the extreme textualists upon whom rational reflection weighed heavily, and the Mu'tazila and all other sects—were unable to reveal. Imam Taj al-Din al-Subki says: Know that al-Ash'ari 'did not originate an opinion nor did he establish a madhhab, but rather he is a reaffirmer of the madhhabs of the Salaf, a fighter for what the Companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, were upon. So affiliation to him is on the basis that he adhered to that.'
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is an editorial introduction explaining the significance of Imam al-Ash'ari and defending his methodological position. The author begins by stating that his hesitation to present this edition stems from his awareness of the depth and breadth of al-Ash'ari's legacy: his many works covering all branches of knowledge, especially kalam (the science of creed), which he revolutionized by correcting the disturbances in Islamic thought. At that time, creedal sciences (both fundamentals and branches) were in danger of deviating from the Qur'an, Sunnah, and the way of the Salaf, largely due to the extremes of the Mu'tazila and the ultra-literalists (ghulat al-nassiyyin). The author then argues that whoever reads al-Ash'ari's 'Maqalat' will see his precise critical engagement with each issue, revealing his comprehensive knowledge and his evaluating everything against a single criterion: 'what the Prophet, his Companions, and the Salaf were upon.' This explains why many later imams of kalam rejected the claim that al-Ash'ari founded a new madhhab after leaving the Mu'tazila. The correct understanding, the author states, is that al-Ash'ari presented a fresh articulation of the Salaf's creed and a new method demonstrating the complete harmony between revelation and reason—something the extreme literalists (who found rational thought heavy) and the Mu'tazila (and other sects) had failed to achieve. The passage concludes with a decisive quote from Taj al-Din al-Subki, who says al-Ash'ari neither invented an opinion nor founded a new school; he merely reaffirmed and defended the way of the Salaf and the Companions. Hence, affiliation to him is because he adhered to that path, not because he innovated.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
غلاة النَّصَّيِّين
السلف
النقل والعقل
مقرّر لمذاهب السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imam al-Ash'ari founded a new theological madhhab distinct from the Salaf.
Correction: He only presented a new articulation of the Salaf's creed and demonstrated harmony between revelation and reason, reaffirming their path.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the correct view of Imam al-Ash'ari's work after he left the Mu'tazila?
A) He established a completely new madhhab in creed.
B) He presented a new articulation of the Salaf's creed and demonstrated harmony between revelation and reason.
C) He rejected rational theology entirely.
D) He returned to the position of the extreme textualists.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari's project was to defend and systematically articulate the creed of the Salaf, not to found a new school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a perceived conflict between a religious text and rational thought, do you tend to reject reason (like the extreme textualists) or prioritize it over revelation (like the Mu'tazila)? Al-Ash'ari's method calls for harmony. Which tendency do you need to correct, and what specific step will you take this week to practice that balance?
?
This lesson shows that al-Ash'ari's project was not to innovate but to reaffirm the Salaf's creed. Are there areas in your faith where you have unknowingly adopted 'new' interpretations that stray from the path of the Salaf? How will you verify that your beliefs align with what the Prophet, his Companions, and the Salaf were upon?
?
Al-Ash'ari's entire effort was to defend the creed of the Salaf using a method that harmonizes reason and revelation. Have you ever considered your own responsibility in defending the correct creed? If you were challenged to explain the harmony between a revealed truth and a rational doubt, would you be prepared? Commit to studying one aspect of your creed this week with the aim of being able to defend it with both text and reason.

Life of Imam al-Ashari
intermediate
4 min
Al-Ash'ari's Comprehensive Methodology
Al-Ash'ari's method: evaluating knowledge by Salafi principle and harmonizing reason and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari's methodology was rooted in the Salafi principle and how he demonstrated the harmony between reason and revelation.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's method: evaluate all knowledge by the Salaf's standard, harmonizing reason with revelation.

This lesson explores the first part of a defense of Imam al-Ash'ari. The author urges us to study al-Ash'ari's works to see his comprehensive knowledge and his critical evaluation of the sciences of his time. The passage establishes that al-Ash'ari did not present a new madhhab but a fresh exposition of Salafi doctrines, demonstrating the perfect harmony between transmitted revelation and reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then the translation. Pay attention to the key phrase 'ما كان عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وصحابته وسلف الأمة' — what the Prophet, his Companions, and the Salaf were upon.
2
Identify the main claim
The author argues against those who say al-Ash'ari created a new madhhab. Instead, he presented 'عرض جديد لعقائد السلف' — a new presentation of Salafi doctrines. Why is this distinction important?
This refutes the common misconception that al-Ash'ari innovated in theology.
3
Understand the harmony argument
Notice that al-Ash'ari's methodology revealed the complete harmony between naql and aql. Who failed to see this? The passage mentions 'غلاة النصيين' (textual extremists) and the Mu'tazila.
This shows that Ash'ari theology bridges reason and revelation, avoiding extremes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَن يقرأ كتاب مجرَّد مقالات الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري» أو يستعرض فهرس مسائله، التي كان للإمام في كل مسألة منها موقف نقدي دقيق - يدرك إحاطة هذا الإمام بمعارفِ عصره وعلومه، وتقييمها والحكم لها أو عليها في ضوء خلفية علمية ثابتة يمكن تلخيصها في كلمة واحدة هي: «ما كان عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وصحابته وسلف الأمة» . ولعل هذا ما يفسر لنا رفض كثيرين من أئمة الكلام» أن يُقال عن الإمام الأشعري» : إنَّه بعد أن تحرَّرَ من ربقة المعتزلة طالَعَ الناسَ بمذهب جديد في العقائد والصحيحُ : أنه طالعهم بعرض جديد لعقائد السَّلف، وبمنهج جديد أيضًا كشف فيه الاتساق الكامل، في الواقع ونفس الأمر بين النقل والعقل، والذي عجز عن كشفه هؤلاء الذين أشرنا إليهم من غُلاة النَّصَّيِّين مِمَّن ثَقُل عليهم النظرُ العقلي ، والمعتزلة وسائرِ الفِرَقِ الأخرى . يقول الإمام تاج الدين السبكي : اعلم أنَّ الأشعري «لم يُبدع رأيًا ولم يُنشئ مذهبًا، وإنما هو مقرّر لمذاهبِ السَّلفِ مُناضِلٌ عما كانت عليه صحابه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فالانتساب إليه باعتبار أنه تَمَسَّك به وأقام الحُجَج والبراهين عليه ؛ فصار المقتدي به السالك سبيله في الدلائل يسمّى أشعريَّا » . وإذا كان لي من إشارة خاطفة تلفت النظر، أو تُسَوِّعُ إعادة نشر كتاب اللمع بهذا التحقيق الدقيق، وبالمقدمة الضافية، والملاحق النادرة التي أتحفنا بها المُحقِّقُ - فهي أن هذا المذهب هو أحوج ما يحتاج المسلمون معرفته اليوم ؛ للخروج من هذه الفتنة الملعونة التي انزلق إليها المسلمون وهم لا يشعرون، وأعني بها : فتنة «التكفير» الذي هو بَريدُ الدِّماءِ واستحلالِ الأموالِ والأعراض، ولا يوجد مذهب من المذاهب العقدية، التي نزلت إلى واقع الأمة وتحرَّكت على أرضها سَلِمَ من الإقدام على تكفير المسلمين، غير مذهب الإمام الأشعري الذي أحيا به ما كان عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وهذه «مسألةٌ تنبّه إليها قدماء الأئمة، ونبّهوا إليها بعد أن عانوا ما عانوا من فتنة المعتزلة، وفتنة الحنابلة، وفتنة الخوارج، وفتنة تسييس التشيع، وأرجو ألا أكونَ مُبالغا لو قلت : إنه بعينه ما تعانيه الأَمَّةُ الإسلامية اليوم، وتدفع ثَمَنَه غاليًا من دمائها وأشلائها وتفرقها، وفقرها، وشتاتها، وذلك بعدما أُحكمت معارك التصدي للمذهب الأشعري ومحاصرته والإساءة إليه، وقد لا يعلم القارئ الكريم أن الإحصاءات الحديثة تقول : إن أهل السُّنَّة يمثلون ما يقرُبُ من ٩٠٪ من مجموع المسلمين في العالم، منهم ما لا يقل عن ٩٠٪ (۱) . (۱) «طبقات الشافعية : ٣٦٥/٣ (بتصرف يسير).
Whoever reads the book 'Mujarrad Maqalat al-Shaykh Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' or reviews its index of issues, for each of which the Imam had a precise critical stance, will realize this Imam's comprehensive knowledge of the knowledge and sciences of his era, and his evaluation of them and judgment for or against them in light of a firm scholarly background that can be summarized in one phrase: 'what the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, his Companions, and the Salaf of the Ummah were upon.' Perhaps this explains for us the rejection by many of the 'Imams of Kalam' of saying about Imam al-Ash'ari that after he freed himself from the yoke of the Mu'tazila he presented the people with a new madhhab in doctrines. The correct view is that he presented them with a new presentation of the doctrines of the Salaf, and with a new methodology as well, in which he revealed the complete harmony, in reality and truth, between transmitted revelation and reason, which those we referred to from among the extremists of the textualists who found rational inquiry burdensome, and the Mu'tazila and all other sects, were unable to uncover. Imam Taj al-Din al-Subki says: Know that al-Ash'ari did not originate an opinion nor did he establish a madhhab; rather he is a consolidator of the madhhabs of the Salaf, a defender of what the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, were upon. Affiliation to him is because he adhered to it and established proofs and evidences for it; so the one who follows him, treading his path in evidences, is called Ash'ari. And if I may have a brief remark to draw attention, or to justify re-publishing the book 'al-Luma'' with this precise editing, with the comprehensive introduction and rare appendices with which the editor has favored us, it is that this madhhab is what Muslims most need to know today, to emerge from this accursed tribulation into which Muslims have slipped without realizing it. I mean by it the tribulation of 'takfir' (excommunication), which is the herald of bloodshed and the legalization of wealth and honor. There is no doctrinal madhhab among those that have descended into the reality of the Ummah and moved on its soil that has remained safe from embarking on takfir of Muslims, except the madhhab of Imam al-Ash'ari, by which he revived what the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was upon. And this is an issue that the early imams paid attention to and alerted to, after they had suffered what they suffered from the tribulation of the Mu'tazila, the tribulation of the Hanabila, the tribulation of the Khawarij, and the tribulation of the politicization of Shi'ism. I hope I am not exaggerating if I say: It is exactly what the Islamic Ummah suffers today, paying dearly for it with its blood, limbs, division, poverty, and fragmentation, after the battles of confronting the Ash'ari madhhab, besieging it, and slandering it were intensified. The noble reader may not know that modern statistics say: Ahl al-Sunna represent close to 90% of all Muslims in the world, and at least 90% of them (are Ash'aris). (1) 'Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya' 3/365 (with slight paraphrase).
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is an editorial preface defending Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his methodology, arguing that he did not innovate a new school but rather revived the creed of the Salaf. The author begins by urging the reader to study al-Ash'ari's works to appreciate his comprehensive knowledge and his critical approach to the ideas of his time, all in light of the principle 'what the Prophet, his Companions, and the Salaf were upon.' He then explains that many scholars of kalam rejected the claim that al-Ash'ari brought a new madhhab after leaving the Mu'tazila; the correct view is that he presented a fresh exposition of Salafi doctrines and a new method demonstrating the harmony between revelation and reason—something the textual extremists and the Mu'tazila failed to do. The author cites Taj al-Din al-Subki, who states that al-Ash'ari did not originate a new opinion or madhhab but was a consolidator of the Salaf's doctrines and a defender of the Companions' way; affiliation to him is because he adhered to that path and established proofs for it. The author then adds his own remark: the Ash'ari madhhab is the most needed today to escape the fitna of takfir (excommunication), which leads to bloodshed and violation of rights. He claims that no other doctrinal school has refrained from takfir except the Ash'ari school. He notes that early imams recognized this after experiencing tribulations from the Mu'tazila, Hanabila, Khawarij, and politicized Shi'ism. The author warns that the Ummah now suffers the same calamities after campaigns against the Ash'ari school, and he cites statistics that about 90% of Muslims are Ahl al-Sunna, most of whom are Ash'aris.

Key Terms
الأشعري
السلف
النقل والعقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imam al-Ash'ari invented a new theological school after leaving the Mu'tazila.
Correction: According to the passage, al-Ash'ari presented a new exposition of the doctrines of the Salaf and a methodology showing harmony between reason and revelation, not a new madhhab.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view of Imam al-Ash'ari's contribution?
A) He created an entirely new theological school after leaving the Mu'tazila.
B) He presented a new exposition of Salafi doctrines using a new methodology.
C) He rejected both reason and revelation in favor of pure tradition.
D) He was a follower of the Mu'tazila throughout his life.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari's methodology was not innovative in doctrine but in presentation: he systematically showed that Salafi creed is fully rational and harmonizes with revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a new idea in religion, do you instinctively measure it against what you have learned from reason alone, or do you first check it against the standard of the Salaf? What would it take for you to truly submit your intellect to their guidance? This week, pick one of your deeply held beliefs and trace it back to whether it actually comes from the Salaf or from your own preference.
?
You have a mind that reasons and a heart that holds revelation. Which one tends to dominate in times of conflict? Are you more like the textualists who ignore reason, or the Mu'tazila who override revelation? Be honest: when was the last time you felt a tension between the two? Instead of avoiding it, will you seek the harmony that al-Ash'ari uncovered—not by dismissing either, but by anchoring both in the Salaf's way?
?
Al-Ash'ari gave his whole life to studying and defending the creed of the Salaf, not his own ideas. How much of your religious knowledge is built on actually reading the words of the Salaf versus relying on contemporary sources? If you had to defend the Salafi creed using their own words, could you? This week, commit to reading one primary Salaf text to check if your understanding aligns with theirs.

Life of Imam al-Ashari
intermediate
4 min
Al-Ash'ari as a Consolidator of Salafi Creed
Al-Subki's statement: al-Ash'ari consolidated Salafi doctrines, not innovated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Taj al-Din al-Subki's statement that al-Ash'ari did not originate a new opinion but consolidated the madhhab of the Salaf.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari is not a founder but a consolidator and defender of the Salafi way.

In this lesson, we examine a key quotation from Imam Taj al-Din al-Subki, a later Ash'ari scholar. Al-Subki clarifies the nature of al-Ash'ari's contribution: he did not create a new madhhab but rather systematized and defended the beliefs of the Salaf. This passage is crucial for understanding the Ash'ari school's self-perception.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic quote from al-Subki and its translation. Note his words: 'لم يبدع رأيًا ولم ينشئ مذهبًا' — he did not innovate an opinion nor establish a madhhab.
2
Analyze al-Subki's claim
Al-Subki says al-Ash'ari is 'مقرر لمذاهب السلف مناضل عما كانت عليه صحابة رسول الله'. What does it mean to be a consolidator and defender?
This emphasizes continuity with the Salaf.
3
Reflect on affiliation
Al-Subki explains that affiliation to al-Ash'ari is because he adhered to the Salafi path and provided proofs. So being called 'Ash'ari' means following that method, not a separate sect.
This addresses the misconception of sectarianism.

ومَن يقرأ كتاب مجرَّد مقالات الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري» أو يستعرض فهرس مسائله، التي كان للإمام في كل مسألة منها موقف نقدي دقيق - يدرك إحاطة هذا الإمام بمعارفِ عصره وعلومه، وتقييمها والحكم لها أو عليها في ضوء خلفية علمية ثابتة يمكن تلخيصها في كلمة واحدة هي: «ما كان عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وصحابته وسلف الأمة» . ولعل هذا ما يفسر لنا رفض كثيرين من أئمة الكلام» أن يُقال عن الإمام الأشعري» : إنَّه بعد أن تحرَّرَ من ربقة المعتزلة طالَعَ الناسَ بمذهب جديد في العقائد والصحيحُ : أنه طالعهم بعرض جديد لعقائد السَّلف، وبمنهج جديد أيضًا كشف فيه الاتساق الكامل، في الواقع ونفس الأمر بين النقل والعقل، والذي عجز عن كشفه هؤلاء الذين أشرنا إليهم من غُلاة النَّصَّيِّين مِمَّن ثَقُل عليهم النظرُ العقلي ، والمعتزلة وسائرِ الفِرَقِ الأخرى . يقول الإمام تاج الدين السبكي : اعلم أنَّ الأشعري «لم يُبدع رأيًا ولم يُنشئ مذهبًا، وإنما هو مقرّر لمذاهبِ السَّلفِ مُناضِلٌ عما كانت عليه صحابه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فالانتساب إليه باعتبار أنه تَمَسَّك به وأقام الحُجَج والبراهين عليه ؛ فصار المقتدي به السالك سبيله في الدلائل يسمّى أشعريَّا » . وإذا كان لي من إشارة خاطفة تلفت النظر، أو تُسَوِّعُ إعادة نشر كتاب اللمع بهذا التحقيق الدقيق، وبالمقدمة الضافية، والملاحق النادرة التي أتحفنا بها المُحقِّقُ - فهي أن هذا المذهب هو أحوج ما يحتاج المسلمون معرفته اليوم ؛ للخروج من هذه الفتنة الملعونة التي انزلق إليها المسلمون وهم لا يشعرون، وأعني بها : فتنة «التكفير» الذي هو بَريدُ الدِّماءِ واستحلالِ الأموالِ والأعراض، ولا يوجد مذهب من المذاهب العقدية، التي نزلت إلى واقع الأمة وتحرَّكت على أرضها سَلِمَ من الإقدام على تكفير المسلمين، غير مذهب الإمام الأشعري الذي أحيا به ما كان عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وهذه «مسألةٌ تنبّه إليها قدماء الأئمة، ونبّهوا إليها بعد أن عانوا ما عانوا من فتنة المعتزلة، وفتنة الحنابلة، وفتنة الخوارج، وفتنة تسييس التشيع، وأرجو ألا أكونَ مُبالغا لو قلت : إنه بعينه ما تعانيه الأَمَّةُ الإسلامية اليوم، وتدفع ثَمَنَه غاليًا من دمائها وأشلائها وتفرقها، وفقرها، وشتاتها، وذلك بعدما أُحكمت معارك التصدي للمذهب الأشعري ومحاصرته والإساءة إليه، وقد لا يعلم القارئ الكريم أن الإحصاءات الحديثة تقول : إن أهل السُّنَّة يمثلون ما يقرُبُ من ٩٠٪ من مجموع المسلمين في العالم، منهم ما لا يقل عن ٩٠٪ (۱) . (۱) «طبقات الشافعية : ٣٦٥/٣ (بتصرف يسير).
Whoever reads the book 'Mujarrad Maqalat al-Shaykh Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' or reviews its index of issues, for each of which the Imam had a precise critical stance, will realize this Imam's comprehensive knowledge of the knowledge and sciences of his era, and his evaluation of them and judgment for or against them in light of a firm scholarly background that can be summarized in one phrase: 'what the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, his Companions, and the Salaf of the Ummah were upon.' Perhaps this explains for us the rejection by many of the 'Imams of Kalam' of saying about Imam al-Ash'ari that after he freed himself from the yoke of the Mu'tazila he presented the people with a new madhhab in doctrines. The correct view is that he presented them with a new presentation of the doctrines of the Salaf, and with a new methodology as well, in which he revealed the complete harmony, in reality and truth, between transmitted revelation and reason, which those we referred to from among the extremists of the textualists who found rational inquiry burdensome, and the Mu'tazila and all other sects, were unable to uncover. Imam Taj al-Din al-Subki says: Know that al-Ash'ari did not originate an opinion nor did he establish a madhhab; rather he is a consolidator of the madhhabs of the Salaf, a defender of what the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, were upon. Affiliation to him is because he adhered to it and established proofs and evidences for it; so the one who follows him, treading his path in evidences, is called Ash'ari. And if I may have a brief remark to draw attention, or to justify re-publishing the book 'al-Luma'' with this precise editing, with the comprehensive introduction and rare appendices with which the editor has favored us, it is that this madhhab is what Muslims most need to know today, to emerge from this accursed tribulation into which Muslims have slipped without realizing it. I mean by it the tribulation of 'takfir' (excommunication), which is the herald of bloodshed and the legalization of wealth and honor. There is no doctrinal madhhab among those that have descended into the reality of the Ummah and moved on its soil that has remained safe from embarking on takfir of Muslims, except the madhhab of Imam al-Ash'ari, by which he revived what the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was upon. And this is an issue that the early imams paid attention to and alerted to, after they had suffered what they suffered from the tribulation of the Mu'tazila, the tribulation of the Hanabila, the tribulation of the Khawarij, and the tribulation of the politicization of Shi'ism. I hope I am not exaggerating if I say: It is exactly what the Islamic Ummah suffers today, paying dearly for it with its blood, limbs, division, poverty, and fragmentation, after the battles of confronting the Ash'ari madhhab, besieging it, and slandering it were intensified. The noble reader may not know that modern statistics say: Ahl al-Sunna represent close to 90% of all Muslims in the world, and at least 90% of them (are Ash'aris). (1) 'Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya' 3/365 (with slight paraphrase).
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is an editorial preface defending Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his methodology, arguing that he did not innovate a new school but rather revived the creed of the Salaf. The author begins by urging the reader to study al-Ash'ari's works to appreciate his comprehensive knowledge and his critical approach to the ideas of his time, all in light of the principle 'what the Prophet, his Companions, and the Salaf were upon.' He then explains that many scholars of kalam rejected the claim that al-Ash'ari brought a new madhhab after leaving the Mu'tazila; the correct view is that he presented a fresh exposition of Salafi doctrines and a new method demonstrating the harmony between revelation and reason—something the textual extremists and the Mu'tazila failed to do. The author cites Taj al-Din al-Subki, who states that al-Ash'ari did not originate a new opinion or madhhab but was a consolidator of the Salaf's doctrines and a defender of the Companions' way; affiliation to him is because he adhered to that path and established proofs for it. The author then adds his own remark: the Ash'ari madhhab is the most needed today to escape the fitna of takfir (excommunication), which leads to bloodshed and violation of rights. He claims that no other doctrinal school has refrained from takfir except the Ash'ari school. He notes that early imams recognized this after experiencing tribulations from the Mu'tazila, Hanabila, Khawarij, and politicized Shi'ism. The author warns that the Ummah now suffers the same calamities after campaigns against the Ash'ari school, and he cites statistics that about 90% of Muslims are Ahl al-Sunna, most of whom are Ash'aris.

Key Terms
الأشعري
السلف
أئمة الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari innovated a new set of beliefs that differed from the Salaf.
Correction: Al-Subki states that al-Ash'ari did not innovate but consolidated and defended the existing doctrines of the Salaf.

Checkpoint
According to Taj al-Din al-Subki, what was al-Ash'ari's role?
A) He founded a new theological school with novel doctrines.
B) He was a consolidator and defender of the doctrines of the Salaf.
C) He rejected all previous scholarship and started from scratch.
D) He was a follower of the Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari did not create a new sect; he systematized and defended the creed of the Salaf, and affiliation to him is based on methodology, not novelty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a scholar who uses logic or rational argumentation to defend Islam, do you instinctively distrust them? After reading al-Subki's clarification, how will you change your initial judgment?
?
Think of a time you labeled someone as misguided because of their method of argument, even though they upheld the same core beliefs as you. How can you emulate al-Ash'ari's role as a consolidator—building bridges rather than dividing?
?
Al-Ash'ari's followers were named after him because they adopted his methodological approach. Is your affiliation to a group or scholar based on loyalty to a person or to the truth they represent? What one step can you take today to ensure your adherence is to the Salafi truth, not mere partisanship?

Life of Imam al-Ashari

The Ash'ari Madhhab's Role in Preventing Takfir
The Ash'ari madhhab as the only school that avoids takfir, with historical and contemporary implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari madhhab is presented as uniquely capable of countering the fitna of takfir and the historical context of this claim.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari school alone among theological movements refrained from excommunicating fellow Muslims.

This lesson examines the final part of the passage, where the author argues for the contemporary relevance of the Ash'ari madhhab. He identifies the greatest tribulation facing the ummah today as takfir (excommunication) and asserts that only the Ash'ari school has consistently avoided this extremism. He lists previous tribulations that early imams warned about and connects them to current crises.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage about the fitna of takfir and the author's claims. Notice the list of tribulations: فتنة المعتزلة, فتنة الحنابلة, فتنة الخوارج, فتنة تسييس التشيع.
These are historical crises of extremism.
2
Understand the claim of uniqueness
The author says no other doctrinal school that engaged with the ummah remained safe from takfir except the Ash'ari school. Why might this be? Reflect on the earlier lessons about its balanced approach.
3
Connect to present circumstances
The author laments the campaigns against the Ash'ari school and cites statistics about the majority of Muslims being Ash'ari. How does this support his argument?
It suggests that attacking Ash'arism harms the unity of the ummah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All theological schools are equally prone to excommunication (takfir).
Correction: The author argues that the Ash'ari school uniquely refrained from takfir, while other schools engaged in it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a unique feature of the Ash'ari madhhab?
A) It was the first to introduce rational argumentation.
B) It remained safe from engaging in takfir of Muslims.
C) It rejected all use of reason in theology.
D) It was the largest school in the early centuries.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari madhhab is uniquely positioned to counter the fitna of takfir because of its historical record and its balanced methodology.

?
Have you ever, even in your heart, considered another Muslim less of a believer because of a disagreement over a branch of faith? How does the author's description of takfir as 'the herald of bloodshed' make you rethink those judgments? What step will you take today to purify your heart from such thoughts?
?
The author says the Ash'ari madhhab revived what the Prophet was upon, yet many today attack it. If you have harbored suspicions or negative views about Ash'aris, are you willing to revisit your assumptions based on this lesson? What concrete action will you take to learn more about this madhhab before forming an opinion?
?
The statistic says 90% of Ahl al-Sunna are Ash'aris. If you are not from that tradition, how does this challenge your sense of unity with the broader Ummah? Will you actively seek to understand and appreciate the madhhab of the majority, or remain in division?

Life of Imam al-Ashari
beginner

The Need for a New Defense of Sunni Creed
Describes the shift from text-based creed to need for rational defense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical circumstances that necessitated a new rational defense of Sunni creed and the role of prophetic hadith in guiding scholars.

Core Idea
Sunni creed needed rational defense when sects and innovations spread.

This passage from the editor's foreword explains how the early Sunni creed relied mainly on textual transmission. But as new sects arose, ideas became confused, and foreign philosophies were translated, a new systematic presentation became necessary. The Prophet's hadith about scholars protecting the religion provides the foundation for this effort.

Guided Path
1
Read about early Sunni creed
Read the first part of the passage describing how the creed was initially preserved through texts and simple statements without extensive rational argument.
Notice the phrase 'شذرات وفتاوى أو مقالاتٍ مجردة عن الاستدلال'.
2
Identify the changing circumstances
Find the list of sects and external factors that disrupted the earlier state: Mu'tazila, Mujassima, etc., caliphal coercion, translation of Greek philosophy.
These are the challenges that made a new approach necessary.
3
Understand the hadith citation
Read the prophetic hadith about scholars protecting religion from distortion, interpretation, and false claims. Reflect on how it justifies the need for a new defense.
The hadith is used as a basis for the scholarly response.
4
Synthesize the need
Combine the early state, the changes, and the hadith to understand why a 'new presentation' of the creed was required.
This sets the stage for the emergence of Imam al-Ash'ari.

اللمع في الرد على أَهْلِ الزَّيْغِ والبدع ... فَقدَّمَ -رحمه الله : «الصياغة العلمية المتكامِلَة، لعقائدِ أهل السنة والجماعة»، ومواقفهم الفكرية، مدعومة بأدلة العقل والنقل بعد أن كانت في غالب الأمر شذرات وفتاوى أو مقالاتٍ مجردةً عن الاستدلال والاحتجاج العقلي، اعتمادًا على النصوص الدينية، إلهية كانت أو نبويَّةً، كما كان الحال في القرون الفاضلة من الصحابة والتابعين وتابعيهم - رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين . فلما تغيّرت الأحوال، وظهرتِ المذاهب والفرقُ : من المعتزلة، والمجسمة، والكرَّامية، والمُعطلة، والخوارجُ مِنْ قَبلِ هؤلاء جميعًا ، وراجَتْ البدعُ وتبلبلت الأفكار .. ومال بعض خلفاء بني العباس إلى بعض هذه الأفكار، بل حاول إكراه الناس على اعتناقها. وتحرَّك أهل الملل الأخرى يُرَوِّجُونَ لمقالاتهم، وتُرجمت الفلسفة الإغريقية، والمذاهب الشرقية، لما حدث هذا كله، مَسَّتِ الحاجةُ إلى عَرْضِ جديد للعقيدة الصحيحة، المستمدة من الكتاب والسُّنَّةِ ، وما أجمع عليه أهل السنة والجماعة»، والرد على بدع المخالفين، وانحرافاتِ الزائغين ؛ عملا بقول النبي -صلى الله عليه وسلم عن علماء أمته : يَرِثُ هذا العِلم، من كلِّ خَلَفٍ (أي جيل) عُدُولُه ، يَنْفُون عنه تحريفَ الغَالينَ، وتأويل الجاهِلينَ، وانتحال المبطلين (۱) رواه البيهقي في سننه [(۲۰۹/۱۰) حديث رقم : ٢١٤٣٩)]. فمن ثُمَّ كان ظهور أبي الحسن الأشعري، في مطلع القرن الرابع الهجري، بأعماله العلميَّة، وأسئلته ومجادلاته، ورسائله ورحلاته ؛ نصرًا لدين الله عز وجل وحماية للأمة من تلك الأحوال الحَرِجَةِ عدها أحدُ مَوْرِّخِي الفكر الإسلامي السابقين - وهو الإمام أبو بكر ابن العربي، الفقيه المالكي الأندلسي الإشبيلي- إحدى القواصم»، في كتابه الشهير العواصم من القواصم(۱)، لولا ظهور أبي الحسن ؛ إذ يقول : ولم يتعرض لحماية الدين إلا آحاد ، اختارهم الله له، له ، ونَصَّبَهُم للذب عنه، فأولهم أبو الحسن الأشعري... وتواتر بعده الأصحاب في الأعقاب على الأعقاب؛ فحفظ الله دينه على من أراد هدايته، فلم يبق وجه من البيان إلا أوضحوه ... وَانتَدَبَ إلى كتاب الله فشرحه، في خمسمِئَةِ مجلد، وسماه بـ (المُخْتَزنَ)، فمنه أخذ الناسُ كُتبهم . . (۲) هذا، وقد وافقه في أقواله ومنهجه في الجُملة، وانتصاره لمواقفِ أهل السنة والجماعة الاعتقادية، المعتمدة على الكتاب والسنة، والاستدلال العقلي والنظر الفكري، والرد على المخالفين سواء كانوا عقليين غلاةً، أو نصيين متشددين- بمنهج جامع متكامل، وروح وسطية سديدة، دون لقاء مباشر، أو تواصل شخصي، ومع اختلافِ الأحوالِ، فيما وراء النهر، عنها في البصرة
Al-Luma' in refutation of the people of deviation and innovation ... So he presented - may Allah have mercy on him - 'the complete scientific formulation of the doctrines of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah' and their intellectual positions, supported by proofs of reason and transmission, after they had for the most part been fragments, fatwas, or articles stripped of rational inference and argumentation, relying on religious texts, whether divine or prophetic, as was the case in the virtuous centuries of the Companions, Followers, and their successors - may Allah be pleased with them all. Then when conditions changed, and the sects and groups appeared: the Mu'tazila, the Mujassima, the Karramiyya, the Mu'aṭṭila, and the Khawarij before all of these; and innovations spread and ideas became confused ... and some Abbasid caliphs inclined to some of these ideas, even attempting to coerce people into adopting them. And people of other religions moved to promote their doctrines, and Greek philosophy and Eastern sects were translated. When all this happened, the need arose for a new presentation of the correct creed, derived from the Book and the Sunnah and what Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah have agreed upon, and refutation of the innovations of opponents and the deviations of deviants; in accordance with the saying of the Prophet - may Allah bless him and grant him peace - concerning the scholars of his nation: 'This knowledge will be inherited by the just ones of every generation (i.e., every era); they will repel from it the distortion of the extremists, the interpretation of the ignorant, and the false claims of the falsifiers' (1) narrated by al-Bayhaqi in his Sunan [(10/209) hadith number: 21439)]. Then from that came the emergence of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, at the beginning of the fourth century AH, with his scholarly works, questions, debates, epistles, and travels; as a victory for the religion of Allah Almighty and a protection for the Ummah from those critical circumstances, which one of the earlier historians of Islamic thought - namely Imam Abu Bakr ibn al-'Arabi, the Maliki jurist from Andalusia and Seville - counted among 'the destructive calamities', in his famous book 'al-'Awāṣim min al-Qawāṣim' (1). Had it not been for the appearance of Abu al-Hasan; for he says: 'None undertook the protection of religion except a few individuals whom Allah chose for it and appointed for defense, the first of whom was Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari... Then companions followed one after another through generations; thus Allah preserved His religion for whomever He desired to guide, and they left no aspect of clarification except that they elucidated it... And he devoted himself to the Book of Allah and explained it in five hundred volumes, calling it 'al-Mukhtazan', and from it people took their books... (2) This, and he was followed in his statements and methodology in general, and his support for the doctrinal positions of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, based on the Book and the Sunnah, rational inference and intellectual reflection, and refutation of opponents whether they were extreme rationalists or rigid textualists - with a comprehensive integrated methodology and a sound moderate spirit, without direct encounter or personal contact, and despite differences of circumstances in Transoxiana from those in Basra.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is an introductory historical narrative from the editor's foreword. It begins by describing the original state of Sunni creed, which was preserved and transmitted based primarily on texts (Qur'an and Sunnah) without extensive rational argumentation. Then it explains the changing circumstances: the rise of various sects (Mu'tazila, Mujassima, Karramiyya, Mu'aṭṭila, Khawarij), the spread of innovations, the influence of some Abbasid caliphs who tried to impose certain ideas, and the translation of Greek philosophy and Eastern doctrines. These developments created a pressing need for a new, systematic presentation of the correct creed—supported by both rational and transmitted proofs—and for refuting the innovations and deviations of opponents. The passage cites a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) about scholars protecting the religion from distortion, interpretation, and false claims. Then it introduces the emergence of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari in the early fourth century AH as a divine provision for this need. It quotes Ibn al-'Arabi's assessment that al-Ash'ari was one of the select individuals Allah chose to defend religion, and that his followers continued the work. It mentions al-Ash'ari's monumental commentary on the Qur'an in five hundred volumes titled 'al-Mukhtazan', from which later scholars derived their books. Finally, it notes that al-Ash'ari's methodology—combining Qur'an, Sunnah, rational deduction, and intellectual reflection—was adopted by later scholars even in different regions like Transoxiana, without direct contact, due to its comprehensive and moderate approach.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
المعتزلة
المجسمة
الكرامية
المعطلة
الخوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Sunni theology always used extensive rational argumentation from the beginning.
Correction: This passage shows that the early approach relied mainly on textual transmission; rational defense became necessary later due to historical challenges.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the main reason for the need for a new presentation of the Sunni creed?
A) The emergence of Imam al-Ash'ari and his followers.
B) The spread of innovations, sects, and the translation of foreign philosophies.
C) The desire of Abbasid caliphs to reform religion.
D) The weakness of earlier scholars in transmitting texts.

Key Takeaway
The need for a rational defense of Sunni creed arose from historical changes including sectarian divisions and foreign influences, and was guided by the prophetic mandate for scholars to protect the religion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever deeply examined the rational basis of your own creed, or have you relied on inherited belief without engaging with the arguments that defending it requires? This lesson shows that scholars built systematic defenses for the truth. What specific step can you take this week to strengthen your understanding of the proofs for your faith?
?
The Prophet ﷺ promised that scholars in every generation would protect the religion from distortion. In your immediate circles, do you see distortions—whether from extremists, ignorant interpretations, or false claims? What is YOUR personal responsibility in preserving the creed as taught by Ahl al-Sunnah, not just in your heart but in how you speak and act?
?
This passage describes how external philosophies and political pressure forced a new presentation of creed. Today, what influences—from media, academia, or society—are shaping how you think about Allah and His religion? Are you aware of them, and are you actively grounding your beliefs in the Qur'an and Sunnah as interpreted by the righteous predecessors, or are you passively absorbing modern assumptions?

Life of Imam al-Ashari
beginner
5 min
The Emergence of Imam al-Ash'ari
Introduces Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his role in defending Sunni creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari emerged as a defender of Sunni creed, his scholarly contributions, and the spread of his methodology.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's emergence was a divine provision to protect the Ummah.

Having established the need for a new defense, this passage introduces Imam al-Ash'ari as the one chosen by Allah to fulfill it. It cites Ibn al-'Arabi's praise, mentions his monumental commentary 'al-Mukhtazan', and notes how his integrated methodology spread even without direct contact.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ash'ari's emergence
Read the passage describing al-Ash'ari's appearance at the beginning of the fourth century AH with his scholarly works and debates.
Note the phrase 'نصرًا لدين الله عز وجل'.
2
Examine Ibn al-'Arabi's testimony
Read the quote from Ibn al-'Arabi considering al-Ash'ari as one of the few protectors of religion.
Ibn al-'Arabi calls the absence of such scholars a 'destructive calamity'.
3
Learn about al-Ash'ari's works
Notice that al-Ash'ari wrote a massive commentary on the Qur'an called 'al-Mukhtazan' in five hundred volumes.
This shows his profound contribution.
4
Understand the spread of his methodology
Read how his approach—combining text, reason, and refutation—was adopted in Transoxiana without direct contact, showing its comprehensive and moderate nature.
This illustrates the universal appeal of his methodology.

The Emergence of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
Describes Ash'ari's historical emergence and his role as a divinely chosen defender.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical circumstances surrounding Ash'ari's emergence and his recognition as a defender of the Sunnah by later scholars.

Core Idea
Ash'ari appeared at a critical time to save Islamic creed from collapse.

In this passage, we learn about the appearance of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari at the beginning of the fourth century. The historian Ibn al-'Arabi considered his arrival as one of the 'calamities' that averted disaster for the Ummah. Here, we explore how Ash'ari's scholarly works and debates protected the religion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the timing
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice that Ash'ari emerged at the start of the fourth Hijri century.
This was a period of theological turmoil.
2
Understand Ibn al-'Arabi's praise
Identify the quote from Ibn al-'Arabi where he calls Ash'ari's appearance one of the 'calamities' that preserved the religion. Reflect on the meaning of 'qawāṣim'.
Ibn al-'Arabi saw Ash'ari as a divinely appointed defender.
3
Notice the mention of al-Mukhtazan
Find the reference to Ash'ari's massive commentary on the Quran, 'al-Mukhtazan', consisting of five hundred volumes.
This shows his deep engagement with scripture.

ومن ثُمَّ كان ظهور أبي الحسن الأشعري، في مطلع القرن الرابع الهجري، بأعماله العلميَّة، وأسئلته ومجادلاته، ورسائله ورحلاته ; عز وجل وحماية للأمة من تلك الأحوال الحَرِجَةِ عدها أحدُ مَوْرِّخِي الفكر الإسلامي السابقين - وهو الإمام أبو بكر ابن العربي، الفقيه المالكي الأندلسي الإشبيلي- إحدى القواصم»، في كتابه الشهير العواصم من القواصم(١)، لولا ظهور أبي الحسن ; إذ يقول : ولم يتعرض لحماية الدين إلا آحاد ، اختارهم الله له، له ، وَنَصَّبَهُم للذب عنه، فأولهم أبو الحسن الأشعري... وتواتر بعده الأصحاب في الأعقاب على الأعقاب؛ فحفظ الله دينه على من أراد هدايته، فلم يبق وجه من البيان إلا أوضحوه ... وانتَدَبَ إلى كتاب الله فشرحه، في خمسمِئَةِ مجلد، وسماه بـ (المُخْتَزنَ)، فمنه أخذ الناسُ كُتبهم . . (٢) هذا، وقد وافقه في أقواله ومنهجه في الجُملة، وانتصاره لمواقفِ أهل السنة والجماعة الاعتقادية، المعتمدة على الكتاب والسنة، الاستدلال العقلي والنظر الفكري، والرد على المخالفين سواء كانوا عقليين غلاةً، أو نصيين متشددين- بمنهج جامع متكامل، وروح وسطية سديدة، دون لقاء مباشر، أو تواصل شخصي، ومع اختلافِ الأحوالِ، فيما وراء النهر، عنها في البصرة وبغداد
Then came the emergence of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari at the beginning of the fourth century Hijri, with his scientific works, his questions and debates, his treatises and travels, to support the religion of God Almighty and to protect the Ummah from those critical circumstances which one of the former historians of Islamic thought—Imam Abu Bakr Ibn al-'Arabi, the Maliki jurist from Andalusia, Seville—considered one of the 'calamities' in his famous book 'al-'Awāṣim min al-Qawāṣim' (1), had it not been for the appearance of Abu al-Hasan; as he said: 'Only individuals, whom God chose and appointed for defense, undertook the protection of the religion, the first of whom was Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari... Then followers succeeded one another generation after generation; God preserved His religion for those whom He desired to guide, and they clarified every aspect of expression... He undertook to explain the Book of God, writing five hundred volumes, and named it 'al-Mukhtazan', from which people took their books (2).' This, and he agreed with him in his statements and his method in general, and his support for the creedal positions of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jamā'ah, which are based on the Book and the Sunnah, rational inference and intellectual reflection, and refuting opponents—whether they were extreme rationalists or rigid textualists—with a comprehensive integrated methodology and a sound moderate spirit, without direct meeting or personal contact, and with different circumstances in Transoxiana compared to those in Basra and Baghdad.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative from the editor's introduction. It begins by stating that Ash'ari emerged at the turn of the fourth century with his scholarly works. It then references the historian Ibn al-'Arabi, who considered Ash'ari's appearance as one of the 'calamities' that prevented the destruction of Islam—meaning that Ash'ari saved the faith by defending it. The passage quotes Ibn al-'Arabi saying that only chosen individuals protected the religion, starting with Ash'ari, and that his followers clarified every aspect. It then mentions Ash'ari's monumental commentary on the Quran called 'al-Mukhtazan', comprising five hundred volumes, from which later scholars drew. The passage next notes that others agreed with Ash'ari's methodology in general, which is based on the Quran and Sunnah, rational inference (al-istidlāl al-'aqlī), and intellectual reflection (al-naẓar al-fikrī). His method refuted both extreme rationalists (like the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya) and rigid textualists (like the literalist Hashwiyya), using a comprehensive, moderate approach. This occurred even though there was no direct contact and the circumstances differed between regions like Transoxiana, Basra, and Baghdad.

Key Terms
المختزن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the name of Ash'ari's multi-volume commentary on the Quran mentioned in this passage?
A) al-‘Awāṣim
B) al-Mukhtazan
C) al-Luma‘
D) Tahdhīb al-Athar

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari's emergence was seen by Ibn al-'Arabi as a divine intervention to protect the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that Allah has chosen you for a specific task to defend His religion? If not, are you willing to be an instrument for His preservation of the faith? What is holding you back?
?
The passage says Ash'ari was one of the few individuals chosen by Allah. What does this say about your own responsibility to seek truth and defend it, even if you are not a scholar? How can you contribute to protecting the creed in your environment?
?
Ibn al-'Arabi considered the circumstances before Ash'ari as potential 'calamities' for Islam. In what ways is the creed being threatened today? Are you part of the solution or part of the problem? Commit to one concrete action this week.

The Balanced Methodology of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
Summarizes Ash'ari's comprehensive and moderate methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the balanced methodology of Ash'ari, combining textual evidence with rational inference.

Core Idea
Ash'ari's method harmonized reason and revelation against extremists.

After examining his historical role, we now delve into Ash'ari's actual methodology. This passage describes how his approach was based on the Quran, Sunnah, rational inference, and intellectual reflection, while refuting both extreme rationalists and rigid textualists. His moderate spirit is highlighted.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of his methodology
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the phrases that describe the foundations of his method.
He based his creed on the Book and Sunnah.
2
Identify the two groups he refuted
Find the terms 'extreme rationalists' and 'rigid textualists' in the translation. Understand who they refer to.
He opposed both extremes to maintain balance.
3
Note the role of reason and reflection
Observe that Ash'ari employs 'rational inference' and 'intellectual reflection' as part of his method.
This counters the misconception that he rejected reason.

The Consensus of Sunni Scholars on Ash'ari and Maturidi's Methodology
Describes the agreement between Ash'ari and Maturidi, and the widespread acceptance of their theology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Sunni scholarly consensus coalesced around the moderate theological methodology of Ash'ari and Maturidi, and the historical factors that led to its widespread acceptance.

Core Idea
Over 90% of Muslims united on the moderate theology of Ash'ari, Maturidi, and their followers.

This passage from the introduction to Al-Luma' explains how the theological school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari found agreement with Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, and how together their approach became the dominant Sunni position. The text highlights key scholars who contributed to this consensus and describes the decline of opposing groups.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping to analyse. Let the flow of historical narrative sink in.
2
Identify the key figures
List the scholars mentioned: al-Maturidi, al-Tahawi, Ibn Abi Zayd, Sahnun. Notice how they are linked across regions.
3
Understand the opponents
The passage mentions groups whose views were rejected: Jahmiyyah, Mu'tazila, Bāṭiniyya, extreme Shia. What do these have in common?
They are all considered innovators by the Sunni mainstream.
4
Reflect on the outcome
The passage claims that over 90% of Muslims united on this moderate position. Consider how this consensus was achieved and its significance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللمع في الرد على أَهْلِ الزَّيْغِ والبدع مما يقطعُ أنها حاجة العصر، ومطلب الفكر في زمنهما ; نقُولُ : وافقَهُ الإمام أبو منصور الماتريدي، [٣٣٣هـ]، الذي وافق أبا الحسن كما قلنا في المواقف والآراء، والمنهج، والاستدلال .. حتى إنه مع تأليفه كتاب «التوحيد»، ألف أيضًا في التفسير كتابه الشهير «تأويلات أهل السنة»، وكلاهما طبع محققا في العقود الأخيرة بإستانبول، وكل أولئك يتزامن مع الجهود المماثلة للإمام الطحاوي [٣٢١هـ] في مصر، وقد يأتي في هذا السياق أيضًا أعمال ابن أبي زيد القيرواني، في الجناح الغربي من العالم العربي، ومن قبله سحنون -رحمهم الله جميعا .، وقبَّض الله -سبحانه- برحمته ، وغَيْرته على دينه وحكمته، من أذكياء الأمة وصلحائها، وأهل العلم والفكر فيها، من ناصروا مذهبهما ، وواصلوا جهودهما في نصرة الدين، وحماية أصوله في كل جيل، حتى خفتت أصوات المبتدعين : من غلاة العقليين؛ كالجهمية والمعتزلة ،ومقلديهم، وانكشفت فضائح الباطنية، وتمويهات غلاة التشيع ومتابعيهم ، واجتمعت كلمة الأمة بما لا يقل عن ٩٠ ( تسعين بالمائة) من جماهير المسلمين على هذا الموقف الوسطي السديد لأبي الحسن، وأبي منصور، والطحاوي، وابن أبي زيد وسحنون -رحمهم الله تعالى . وظهرت المؤلفات والكتب والدواوين والمصنفات، موجزة ومبسوطة، وسجّلت أخبارُ الرجال والطبقات، والإجازات والروايات هذه الجهود الفكرية وخاصة في المجالين الأساسيين: أصول الدين ،والعقيدة وأصول الفقه والأحكام
Al-Luma' in Refuting the People of Deviation and Innovation, which confirms that it was a need of the age and an intellectual requirement in their time. We say: Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi [d. 333 AH] agreed with him, who agreed with Abu al-Hasan as we said in positions, views, methodology, and reasoning... to the extent that along with his book 'al-Tawhid', he also authored in tafsir his famous book 'Ta'wilat Ahl al-Sunnah', both of which were published with critical editions in recent decades in Istanbul. All of that coincided with similar efforts of Imam al-Tahawi [d. 321 AH] in Egypt, and in this context also come the works of Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani in the western wing of the Arab world, and before him Sahnun—may God have mercy on them all. And God—glorious and exalted—by His mercy, zeal for His religion, and wisdom, raised up from the intelligent and righteous of the Ummah, and from its scholars and thinkers, those who supported their school and continued their efforts in defending the religion and protecting its principles in every generation, until the voices of innovators fell silent: from the extreme rationalists like the Jahmiyyah and Mu'tazila and their imitators, and the scandals of the Bāṭiniyya and the deceptions of the extreme Shia and their followers were exposed. And the word of the Ummah united, comprising no less than ninety percent of the Muslim masses, upon this sound moderate position of Abu al-Hasan, Abu Mansur, al-Tahawi, Ibn Abi Zayd, and Sahnun—may God have mercy on them. And numerous books, volumes, collections, and compilations appeared, both concise and detailed, and the biographical accounts of men, generations, licenses (ijāzāt), and transmissions recorded these intellectual efforts, especially in the two fundamental fields: the principles of religion (Uṣūl al-Dīn) and creed, and the principles of jurisprudence (Uṣūl al-Fiqh) and rulings.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage continues the editor's historical account. It begins with the title of the book, 'Al-Luma' fi al-Radd 'ala Ahl al-Zaygh wa al-Bida', which is the work being introduced. The editor then states that this book was a necessity of the age. He notes that Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi agreed with Ash'ari's methodology, despite being in different regions. Maturidi wrote 'al-Tawhid' on theology and 'Ta'wilat Ahl al-Sunnah' on Quranic exegesis. These efforts are linked to those of Imam al-Tahawi in Egypt, Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani in the west, and Sahnun before him. The passage then describes how God raised supporters of this theology who defended it until the voices of innovators fell silent: these innovators include extreme rationalists such as the Jahmiyyah and Mu'tazila, as well as the Bāṭiniyya and extreme Shia. As a result, the Muslim community united—over 90%—on the sound moderate position of these five imams. The passage concludes by noting the vast literary output in the fields of usul al-din (principles of religion) and usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence).

الطحاوي
ابن أبي زيد القيرواني
أهل السنة
الموقف الوسطي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools were always in conflict
Correction: This passage emphasizes their agreement in positions, views, methodology, and reasoning, showing they were aligned.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni community united around the moderate theology of Ash'ari and Maturidi, with over 90% acceptance, due to the efforts of scholars who defended it against innovators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Are you, in your current environment, actively defending the principles of the creed, or do you remain silent when you hear deviant ideas? ?
The text says that 'the word of the Ummah united' on this moderate position. Do you feel a sense of belonging to that overwhelming majority, or do you find yourself drawn to fringe opinions that separate you from the main body of Muslims? What would it cost you to humble yourself and fully embrace the consensus?
?
Consider the innovators mentioned—the Jahmiyyah, Mu'tazila, Bāṭiniyya, and extreme Shia—whose 'voices fell silent' due to the scholars' efforts. Are there any whispers of innovation in your own heart or among your close associates that you tolerate because they are familiar? How will you uproot them before they grow?

Modern Scholarship on Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
Historical overview of modern scholarly works on Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the contributions of McCarthy, Gharaba, and Fawqiya to the study of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his works.

Core Idea
Modern scholarship on Ash'ari involves both textual editions and interpretive debates.

This lesson introduces the key modern scholars who have studied the works of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. It focuses on Richard McCarthy's foundational work, the critiques of his edition by Dr. Gharaba, and the subsequent work of Dr. Fawqiya Husayn Mahmoud. Understanding this scholarly context helps appreciate the textual history of Ash'ari's writings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the modern scholarship on Ash'ari.
Notice the names and titles mentioned.
2
Identify the scholars
Identify the three scholars mentioned: McCarthy, Gharaba, and Fawqiya. Note what each contributed according to the passage.
McCarthy's work, Gharaba's critique, Fawqiya's support.
3
Reflect on the debate
Consider how the passage highlights differing interpretations: McCarthy's readings were criticized by Gharaba, and Fawqiya supported McCarthy. This shows scholarly debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عام ١٩٥٣ أيضًا بعنوان 'The Theology Of Al Ashari، وهو دراسة مستفيضة عن أبي الحسن مع ترجمة لبعض نصوصه. ولكن نشرته لكتاب اللمع في بيروت - تضمَّنت بعض القراءات غير الموفقة للنّصّ، ووجهات نظر ناقشها الدكتور غرابة تفصيلا، ثم جاءت بعد ذلك الدكتورة فوقية حسين محمود - الأستاذة بجامعة عين شمس سابقا ، لتناصر رحمها الله - آراء هذا المستشرق في عمل مستفيض لها عن الأشعري وكتابه «الإبانة»، تاليا لعملها الأساسي - في المملكة المتحدة أيضًا - عن الإمام الجويني (٤٧٨هـ) رحم الله الجميع (1)
Also in the year 1953, with the title 'The Theology Of Al-Ash'ari', which is an extensive study of Abu al-Hasan with a translation of some of his texts. But his publication of the book Al-Luma in Beirut included some unsuccessful readings of the text, and viewpoints that Dr. Gharaba discussed in detail. Then after that came Dr. Fawqiya Husayn Mahmoud - formerly a professor at Ain Shams University - may God have mercy on her - supporting the views of this orientalist in an extensive work of hers on al-Ash'ari and his book Al-Ibana, following her foundational work - also in the United Kingdom - on Imam al-Juwayni (d. 478 AH). May God have mercy on all.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a historical summary of modern scholarly works on Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. It begins by mentioning Richard McCarthy's 1953 work 'The Theology of Al-Ash'ari', which includes translations of some of Ash'ari's texts. However, his edition of Al-Luma published in Beirut contained some questionable readings, which were later criticized by Dr. Gharaba. Then it discusses Dr. Fawqiya Husayn Mahmoud's work, which supported McCarthy's orientalist views in her study of Ash'ari and his book Al-Ibana. The passage notes that she was a professor at Ain Shams University and also worked on Imam al-Juwayni. The paragraph ends with a prayer for mercy on all mentioned scholars. The footnote marker (1) indicates a citation to Fawqiya's book.

Key Takeaway
Modern scholarship on al-Ash'ari includes McCarthy's pioneering work, Gharaba's critical response, and Fawqiya's supportive studies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Azhar International Conference and Research Center on Imam al-Ash'ari
Describes the Azhar conference and the establishment of a research center.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major modern scholarly initiatives undertaken by al-Azhar to study and promote the legacy of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
Al-Azhar's conference and research center demonstrate ongoing scholarly engagement with Ash'ari thought.

After learning about the life and methodology of Imam al-Ash'ari, we now turn to how modern institutions continue to study his work. This passage highlights two concrete efforts by al-Azhar in the early 21st century: a major international conference and the founding of a specialized research center. These show that Ash'ari scholarship is not a thing of the past but an active field of study.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the reference to the conference date and the four volumes of proceedings.
2
Identify the two main initiatives
The passage mentions two key actions by al-Azhar: the international conference and the establishment of a research center. List them in your mind.
The conference is described in detail, while the center is mentioned at the end.
3
Consider the participation
Note that the conference included both orientalists and Arab scholars, and that the Grand Imam himself contributed multiple researches.
This shows broad engagement.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why does al-Azhar invest in such efforts? What does this tell us about the relevance of Ash'ari today?
The passage ends by emphasizing that interest has not waned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أبرز هذه الأعمال والجهود الحثيثة الحديثة : المؤتمر الدولي الذي عقده الأزهر الشريف بالقاهرة، في مطلع العقد الرابع من القرن الخامس عشرَ الثاني من القرن الحادي والعشرين الميلادي عن أبي الحسن وشخصيته ومنهجه ومذهبه، وأعماله ومؤلفاته، ونُشِرَت بحوث المؤتمر في أربعة مجلدات كبار وأسهم المشاركون من المستشرقين والعرب ببحوث كثيرة، ومنهم شيخ الأزهر وإمامه الأكبر الدكتور أحمد الطيب، الذي أصدر -حفظه الله - عن الشيخ حتى الآن بحوثا أربعة(٢)، وما نفد معين القول أو ضاق مجال النظر، أو قلت دواعي الاهتمام، بل أقام الأزهر مركزا متخصصا أسماه مركز بحوث الإمام أبي الحسن الأشعري .
And among the most prominent of these continuous works and modern efforts: the international conference held by al-Azhar al-Sharif in Cairo, at the beginning of the fourth decade of the fifteenth [century]? the second of the twenty-first century CE, about Abu al-Hasan, his personality, methodology, school, works, and writings. The conference papers were published in four large volumes, and the participants, both orientalists and Arabs, contributed many researches, among them the Sheikh of al-Azhar and its Grand Imam Dr. Ahmad al-Tayyib, who has produced so far four researches about the Sheikh - may God preserve him. And the wellspring of speech has not dried up, nor has the field of consideration narrowed, nor have the reasons for interest diminished; rather al-Azhar established a specialized center which it named the Center for Research on Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of modern scholarly initiatives regarding Imam al-Ash'ari, focusing on two main institutional efforts by al-Azhar. First, it describes an international conference held in Cairo at the beginning of the fourth decade of the fifteenth century AH (which corresponds to the early 2000s CE). The conference centered on Ash'ari's personality, methodology, school, and works, and its proceedings were published in four large volumes with participation from both orientalists and Arab scholars. Notably, the Grand Imam of al-Azhar, Dr. Ahmad al-Tayyib, contributed four separate researches on Ash'ari. Second, the passage emphasizes that scholarly interest has not waned; instead, al-Azhar established a specialized research center named after Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. The footnote marker (2) likely refers to Tayyib's works. The passage concludes by affirming the continuity of scholarly attention.

Key Terms
الأزهر الشريف
أبو الحسن الأشعري
المؤتمر الدولي
مركز بحوث الإمام أبي الحسن الأشعري
أحمد الطيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Azhar's interest in Ash'ari is merely historical or has ceased.
Correction: The passage shows that al-Azhar not only held a major conference but also established a dedicated research center, indicating active and continuous engagement with Ash'ari thought.

Checkpoint
What did al-Azhar establish after the conference to continue research on Ash'ari?
A) A professorial chair
B) A specialized research center
C) A new university department
D) A journal

Key Takeaway
Al-Azhar's international conference and research center highlight the enduring scholarly engagement with Imam al-Ash'ari's legacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that al-Azhar established a research center dedicated to Imam al-Ash'ari. What specific steps will you take this week to benefit from the works of this center? Do not say 'I will read'—name a concrete action.
?
The Grand Imam personally contributed four researches on Ash'ari. What have you contributed to your own understanding of Ahl al-Sunna's foundations? If nothing, what is the real obstacle in your heart, and how will you remove it starting today?

Life of Imam al-Ashari
beginner
4 min
Biographical Overview of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
Editor presents biographical overview of Ash'ari's life and character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key aspects of Imam al-Ash'ari's life, character, and educational background that prepared him to become a leading theologian.

Core Idea
Imam al-Ash'ari's personality blended piety with scholarly versatility.

This passage from the editor of al-Luma' offers a concise portrait of Imam al-Ash'ari's character and life journey. Before diving into his theological works, the editor highlights his simplicity, moderation, and piety, and then traces his lineage, birthplace, and the scholarly environment that shaped him. This foundation helps appreciate his contributions to kalam and Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall content.
Pay attention to the flow: character traits first, then biographical details.
2
Identify character traits
The passage lists several personal qualities of al-Ash'ari. Find them and note how they are described: simplicity, moderation, piety, good companionship, and ease with students.
These traits reflect his personality as a teacher and scholar.
3
Trace his educational journey
Notice his birth in Basra, later move to Baghdad, and his interaction with various teachers (direct and indirect). Understand how this broad exposure shaped his comprehensive knowledge.
He specialized in kalam despite knowing many fields.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب شخصية أبي الحسن الأشعري :
ربما كان من المناسب، في ختام هذا المدخل التمهيدي – وقبل أن نتعرّض لجوانب تفصيلية من سيرة شيخنا ومسيرته ودوره، وخصائص كتابه «اللمع» - أن نُقدِّم صورة عامة لملامح شخصيته ، التي تتميز بالبساطة والاعتدال والورع، وحسن المعاشرة،
والتبسط مع التلاميذ والأصحاب، مقرونة بشواهد سريعة لكل سمة
من هذه السمات، فيما يلي :
ولد شيخنا علي بن إسماعيل بن أبي بشر إسحاق بن سالم بن إسماعيل بن عبد الله بن بلال بن أبي بردة بن أبي موسى الأشعري، صاحب رسول الله -صلى الله عليه وسلم- في البصرة عام (٢٦٠هـ)، وعاش بها أكثر سني حياته ، ثم انتقل إلى بغداد، وأقام بها حتى لقي ربه، في قرابة الخامسة والستين من العمر، ولقي الكثيرين من الشيوخ في عاصمتي الثقافة الإسلامية حينذاك، وقرأ للكثيرين، وسمع عنهم وإن لم يلقهم، وتأثر بهم ؛ فله شيوخ مباشرون، وشيوخ غير مباشرين . كما يلاحظ أنه عن طريق هؤلاء الشيوخ بنوعيهم، وعن طريق القراءة والدراسة والسماع أيضًا، تيسر له الإلمام بتيارات الفكر الإسلامي المتنوعة، وسائر الاتجاهات والمذاهب في مختلف حقول المعرفة الذائعة في عصره، وإن اختص بعلم الكلام والدراسات العقلية، كما تدل مؤلفاته (۱) ، وإنتاجه العلمي الغزير .
B: The personality of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari: Perhaps it is appropriate, at the conclusion of this preliminary introduction – before we go into detailed aspects of the biography of our shaykh, his career, his role, and the characteristics of his book 'Al-Luma'' – to present a general picture of the features of his personality, which is distinguished by simplicity, moderation, piety, good companionship, and ease with students and companions, accompanied by quick examples for each of these features, as follows: Our shaykh Ali ibn Isma'il ibn Abi Bishr Ishaq ibn Salim ibn Isma'il ibn Abdullah ibn Bilal ibn Abi Burda ibn Abi Musa al-Ash'ari, the companion of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him), was born in Basra in the year 260 AH, and lived there most of his life. Then he moved to Baghdad and resided there until he met his Lord, at about sixty-five years of age. He met many teachers in the two capitals of Islamic culture at that time, read to many, and heard from them even if he did not meet them, and was influenced by them. So he had direct teachers and indirect teachers. It is also observed that through these teachers of both types, and through reading, study, and listening as well, he was able to comprehend the diverse currents of Islamic thought, and all the trends and sects in the various fields of knowledge prevalent in his era, although he specialized in kalam (speculative theology) and rational studies, as his works (1) and his abundant scholarly output indicate.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a biographical overview provided by the editor. It begins by introducing a section on the personality of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, stating that before detailing aspects of his life and works, it is appropriate to give a general picture of his character traits: simplicity, moderation, piety, good companionship, and ease with students and companions. The passage then presents the full lineage of Ash'ari, tracing him back to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, a companion of the Prophet. It mentions that he was born in Basra in 260 AH, lived there most of his life, then moved to Baghdad and died there at about 65. He met many teachers in Basra and Baghdad, studied under them, and was influenced by them, having both direct and indirect teachers. Through these teachers and his own reading and listening, he gained comprehensive knowledge of the various intellectual currents, sects, and fields of knowledge of his time, though he specialized in kalam and rational studies, as evidenced by his works and prolific output.

البصرة
بغداد
شيوخ مباشرون
شيوخ غير مباشرين
علم الكلام

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Ash'ari only studied kalam and was limited in his knowledge.
Correction: This passage shows he was well-versed in many fields of Islamic thought, having studied under various teachers and engaged with diverse currents.

Checkpoint

B) Basra
C) Kufa
D) Damascus

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari's life combined deep piety and broad learning, making him a pivotal figure in Islamic theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Ash'ari combined deep piety with tireless seeking of knowledge. In your own life, where is the balance between your devotion to learning and your spiritual practice? Are you neglecting one for the other? What change will you make today to realign them?
?
He learned from both direct teachers and indirect sources. Are you content with passive learning (videos, books) without seeking a living teacher? What step will you take this week to find a mentor or join a study circle?
?
The passage notes his 'simplicity, moderation, piety, good companionship, and ease with students.' Which of these qualities do you lack most in your interactions with others? Write one concrete action you will take to practice that quality tomorrow.

Life of Imam al-Ashari
beginner
