Al-Bahili: Scholar and Convert
Editor praises al-Bahili's intellect and narrates his conversion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Bahili's dual identity as both a mystic and a logician, and how his debate with al-Ash'ari led to his conversion from Imami Shi'ism.

Core Idea
A scholar's conversion through rational debate highlights the power of proof.

This passage introduces us to Abu al-Hasan al-Bahili, a key figure in early Ash'ari history. The editor warns us not to underestimate him as merely a pious ascetic—he was also a trained logician and mutakallim. More importantly, his conversion from Imami Shi'ism to the Ash'ari school came not through pressure or politics, but through a formal debate with Imam al-Ash'ari himself, in which the truth became undeniable.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for the biographical style. Notice the two main parts: the praise of al-Bahili's intellect and the story of his conversion.
The passage contains two quotations—from al-Dhahabi and Ibn Furak.
2
Identify al-Bahili's two qualities
The editor emphasizes that al-Bahili was not only a devout ascetic but also a scholar of logic and kalam. Find the evidence for both aspects.
Look for the quote from al-Dhahabi about his intelligence and study of logic.
3
Understand the conversion story
Ibn Furak narrates that al-Bahili was originally an Imami (Twelver Shi'a) leader. Note the key term 'alzamahu al-hujja' (forced the proof)—this shows the debate was won by rational argument.
The conversion was a direct result of a munazara (debate).
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why does the editor include this story? It demonstrates that Ash'ari theology was defended through reason, and that even a leader of a rival school could be convinced by evidence.
This lesson highlights the importance of rational argument in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا ولا تظننَّ أيها القارئ أن الباهلي مجرد «درويش» متوله بالذكر والعبادة، فإنه على تنسكه وتولُّهه- كما حكى الباقلاني، يشتغل بعلم المنطق، إلى جوار علم الكلام حتى ليقول عنه الحافظ الذهبي - وهو من غير الأشاعرة بل من نُقَادِهم: «أخذ عن الأشعري علم المنطق، وسمع وتقدم، وكان من أذكياء العالم، مع الدين والتعبد» (۱) . وقال عنه ابن فُورَك - وهو زميل الإسفراييني في التتلمذ للباهلي : ومِمَّنْ تخرج به الضمير يرجع إلى الأشعري- وممَّن اختلف إليه واستفاد منه المعروف بأبي الحسن الباهلي، وكان إماميًا (أي شيعيا اثنا عشريَّا رئيسا مقدمًا، فانتقل من مذهبهم ؛ بمناظرة جرت له مع الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري رضي الله عنه - ألزمه فيها الحجة، حتى بان له الخطأُ فيما كان عليه من مذاهب الإمامية ،فتركها واختلف إليه ونشر علمه بالبصرة، واستفاد منه الخلقُ الكثيرون»(۲)
This, and do not think, O reader, that al-Bahili was merely a 'darvish' absorbed in remembrance and worship, for despite his asceticism and absorption—as al-Baqillani reported—he occupied himself with the science of logic alongside the science of kalam, so much so that al-Hafiz al-Dhahabi—who is not among the Ash'arites but rather among their critics—said about him: 'He took logic from al-Ash'ari, and heard (hadith) and advanced, and was among the most intelligent people in the world, along with religiosity and devotion' (1). And Ibn Furak—who was the colleague of al-Isfarayini in being a student of al-Bahili—said about him: 'And among those who graduated under him (the pronoun referring to al-Ash'ari), and among those who frequented him and benefited from him, was the one known as Abu al-Hasan al-Bahili. He was an Imami (i.e., a Twelver Shi'a, a leader and prominent), but he left their sect due to a debate that took place between him and Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him—in which he forced the proof upon him, until the error in what he was upon of the Imami doctrines became clear to him, so he abandoned them and frequented him and spread his knowledge in Basra, and many people benefited from him' (2).
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note from the editor, highlighting two important aspects of Abu al-Hasan al-Bahili: his intellectual breadth and his conversion. First, the editor warns against underestimating al-Bahili as merely a pious ascetic; he was also a scholar of logic and kalam. This is supported by a quote from al-Dhahabi, who despite being a critic of the Ash'arites, praised al-Bahili's intelligence and religiosity, noting that he studied logic directly under al-Ash'ari. Second, the editor cites Ibn Furak to narrate al-Bahili's conversion from Twelver Shi'ism to the Ash'ari school. The conversion occurred through a formal debate (munazara) with al-Ash'ari himself, in which al-Ash'ari 'forced the proof' (alzamahu al-hujja), convincing al-Bahili of the error of his former doctrines. After converting, al-Bahili became a devoted student and spread Ash'ari teachings in Basra, influencing many. The passage thus underscores both al-Bahili's scholarly credentials and his intellectual honesty in following the truth.

Key Terms
الباهلي
إمامي
اثنا عشري
مناظرة
إلزام الحجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume al-Bahili was only a mystic with no scholarly depth.
Correction: The passage shows he was also a logician and mutakallim, praised by al-Dhahabi for his intelligence and study of logic under al-Ash'ari.

Checkpoint
What caused al-Bahili to abandon his Imami Shi'a beliefs?
A) A dream he had
B) A debate with al-Ash'ari in which he was convinced by the proof
C) The death of his teacher
D) A political decree

Key Takeaway
Al-Bahili's conversion through rational debate exemplifies the Ash'ari commitment to using reason in theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a deeply held belief you have about religion or theology. If someone presented you with a proof that it was wrong, would you be willing to abandon it, or would you cling to it out of habit or community pressure? What does your answer reveal about your commitment to truth?
?
Al-Bahili left his entire community and status as a leader among the Imamiyya after being convinced by a single debate. Is there any belief you hold primarily because of your social circle rather than because you have examined the evidence for yourself? What would it take for you to change?
?
The passage highlights that al-Bahili was both a mystic (darvish) and a logician. Are you forcing yourself to engage with difficult arguments that challenge your worldview, or do you prefer to stay in the comfort of devotional practice without intellectual scrutiny? Where is your balance between heart and mind, and is it honest?

Ibn Khafif al-Shirazi: A Student of al-Ash'ari
Editor introduces Ibn Khafif as a third student of al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biographical connection between Ibn Khafif al-Shirazi and Imam al-Ash'ari, including the historical record of his studies in 300 AH.

Core Idea
Ibn Khafif studied with al-Ash'ari in Basra in 300 AH.

This short passage introduces Ibn Khafif al-Shirazi as the third major student of al-Ash'ari. It highlights his dual identity as a Sufi and Ash'ari theologian and provides a precise historical anchor: the year 300 AH, when he attended al-Ash'ari's hadith lessons in Basra. This notice connects the early Ash'ari school with the Sufi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice that the passage is incomplete—it cuts off mid-sentence. Still, absorb the information provided.
The passage is a biographical snippet from the editor.
2
Identify the key facts
Who is Ibn Khafif? Who recorded his biography? What year is given for his studies with al-Ash'ari?
The biographer is Abu al-Hasan al-Daylami, a student of Ibn Khafif.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why it matters that Ibn Khafif studied hadith with al-Ash'ari, especially given his identity as a Sufi. What does this tell us about the early Ash'ari school?
The date 300 AH is early in al-Ash'ari's career and confirms his teaching activity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثالث التلاميذ هو : الشيخ محمد بن خفيف الشيرازي الصوفي، المتكلّم الأشعري (۳۷۱هـ) وقد سجّل أحد تلامذة ابن خفيف سيرة أستاذه، بعنوان : سيرة الشيخ الكبير بالعربية وهو أبو الحسن الديلمي -رحمه الله - صاحب كتاب «عطفُ الألف المألوف على اللام المعطوف»، سجّل التاريخ الثابت في سياحات ابن خفيف، وهو سنة (٣٠٠هـ)، ففي هذا التاريخ كان في البصرة في أثناء عودته من إحدى مراتِ حجه، ومكث حينا يتابع دروس أبي الحسن الأشعري، في الحديث
And the third student is: Shaykh Muhammad ibn Khafif al-Shirazi al-Sufi, the Ash'ari mutakallim (d. 371 AH). One of the students of Ibn Khafif recorded the biography of his teacher, entitled: 'The Biography of the Great Shaykh in Arabic', and he is Abu al-Hasan al-Daylami—may Allah have mercy on him—author of the book 'The Bending of the Familiar Alif upon the Struck Lam'. He recorded the fixed date in Ibn Khafif's travels, which is the year (300 AH), for in that year he was in Basra during his return from one of his pilgrimages, and he stayed for a while following the lessons of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, in hadith [the text breaks off].
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a brief biographical notice from the editor introducing Muhammad ibn Khafif al-Shirazi as the third prominent student of al-Ash'ari mentioned in this section. He is described as a Sufi and an Ash'ari mutakallim. The editor notes that one of Ibn Khafif's students, Abu al-Hasan al-Daylami, authored a biography of his teacher. In that biography, al-Daylami recorded that in the year 300 AH, Ibn Khafif was in Basra returning from Hajj and stayed to attend al-Ash'ari's lessons in hadith. The passage is cut off, but it establishes Ibn Khafif's direct study with al-Ash'ari. The mention of the year 300 AH provides a chronological anchor: al-Ash'ari was still alive and teaching in Basra at that time.

Correction: The passage shows Ibn Khafif studied kalam and hadith with al-Ash'ari; he was both a Sufi and an Ash'ari theologian.

Ibn Khafif al-Shirazi: The Student Who Turned from Mu'tazilism to Ash'arism
Biographical notice of Ibn Khafif and his meeting with al-Ash'ari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical significance of Ibn Khafif's meeting with al-Ash'ari and his transition from Mu'tazilism to Ash'arism as recorded by his student al-Dailami.

Core Idea
Ibn Khafif's biography documents a key transition from Mu'tazilism to Ash'arism in early 4th century AH.

This passage introduces Muhammad ibn Khafif al-Shirazi, a Sufi and Ash'ari theologian who was a student of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. It highlights his initial Mu'tazili phase and his shift to Ash'arism, as recorded by his student al-Dailami. The account provides valuable insight into the earliest teaching circles of al-Ash'ari in Basra and the transmission of his ideas.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical notice of Ibn Khafif
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the person and his significance.
Focus on the names and dates mentioned.
2
Identify the key details
Note that Ibn Khafif was an Ash'ari mutakallim and a Sufi, that his biography was written by al-Dailami, and that he attended al-Ash'ari's lessons in Basra in the year 300 AH.
The date 300 AH is a fixed historical marker.
3
Understand the doctrinal shift
The biography states that Ibn Khafif began as a Mu'tazili for a short period before separating from them and manifesting his own beliefs, which align with Ash'arism.
This shows that even early students of al-Ash'ari had diverse backgrounds.
4
Recognize the historical value
Al-Subki transmitted Ibn Khafif's account of his first meeting with al-Ash'ari in two versions, considered a valuable document about the earliest lessons and debates of al-Ash'ari in Basra.
This underscores the importance of biographical sources for early Ash'ari history.

وثالث التلاميذ هو : الشيخ محمد بن خفيف الشيرازي الصوفي، المتكلّم الأشعري (۳۷۱هـ). وقد سجّل أحد تلامذة ابن خفيف سيرة أستاذه، بعنوان : سيرة الشيخ الكبير بالعربية وهو أبو الحسن الديلمي -رحمه الله - صاحب كتاب «عطفُ الألف المألوف على اللام المعطوف»، سجّل التاريخ الثابت في سياحات ابن خفيف، وهو سنة (٣٠٠هـ)، ففي هذا التاريخ كان في البصرة في أثناء عودته من إحدى مراتِ حجه، ومكث حينا يتابع دروس أبي الحسن الأشعري، في الحديث بالبصرة، وتصفه الترجمة : ذلك الشيخ الذي بدأ معتزليا لفترة قليلة، ثم انفصل عن المعتزلة وأبدى معتقداته الخاصة»(۱) وفي هذا الخصوص نقل السبكي رواية ابن خفيف للقائه الأول بشيخه أبي الحسن، على وجهين، وتعد – على كل حال – وثيقة قيمة عن أقدم مجالس دروس الأشعري وحواراته بالبصرة.
And the third of the students is: Shaykh Muhammad ibn Khafif al-Shirazi al-Sufi, the Ash'ari mutakallim (371 AH). One of the students of Ibn Khafīf recorded the biography of his teacher, entitled: 'Sirat al-Shaykh al-Kabir' in Arabic, and he is Abu al-Hasan al-Dailami - may Allah have mercy on him - the author of the book 'Atf al-Alif al-Ma'luf ala al-Lam al-Ma'tuf'. He recorded a fixed date in the travels of Ibn Khafif, which is the year (300 AH); for in that date he was in Basra during his return from one of his pilgrimages, and he stayed a while attending the lessons of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari in hadith in Basra. The biography describes him: 'That shaykh who began as a Mu'tazili for a short period, then separated from the Mu'tazila and manifested his own beliefs.' In this regard, al-Subki transmitted Ibn Khafif's report of his first meeting with his shaykh Abu al-Hasan, in two versions, and it is considered – in any case – a valuable document about the earliest sessions of al-Ash'ari's lessons and his debates in Basra.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice on Muhammad ibn Khafif al-Shirazi, the third major student of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari mentioned in this introduction. Ibn Khafif was a Sufi and an Ash'ari theologian who died in 371 AH. The paragraph then turns to his student, Abu al-Hasan al-Dailami, who wrote a biography of Ibn Khafif titled 'Sirat al-Shaykh al-Kabir'. Al-Dailami recorded that in the year 300 AH, Ibn Khafif was in Basra on his way back from hajj and attended the lessons of al-Ash'ari in hadith. The biography describes Ibn Khafif as someone who initially spent a short period as a Mu'tazili but later left Mu'tazilism and expressed his own 'aqidah, which aligns with Ash'arism. The passage further notes that al-Subki (in his Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya) transmitted Ibn Khafif's account of his first meeting with al-Ash'ari in two versions, and these accounts are considered valuable historical documents about the earliest teaching circles and debates of al-Ash'ari in Basra. This highlights the historical significance of Ibn Khafif's testimony for understanding the development of Ash'ari's thought and the transition from Mu'tazilism to Ash'arism.

A Dream Indicating Spiritual Rank
Al-Daylami reports a dream indicating Ibn Khafif's high spiritual station

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a dream anecdote serves to affirm Ibn Khafif's spiritual station and his alignment with Ash'ari creed.

Core Idea
A dream rebuke reveals Ibn Khafif as among the people of certainty.

This short passage from al-Daylami's biography of his shaykh, Ibn Khafif, illustrates a spiritual endorsement through a dream. It shows that Ibn Khafif's creed matched that of Imam al-Ash'ari, and a visionary voice rebuked anyone who would reproach him, affirming his high rank. As you read, consider how dreams function as signs of spiritual status in Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then the English translation. Notice the key elements: the book's content, the dream, and the phrase 'people of certainty'.
The Arabic is straightforward; focus on the dream narrative.
2
Identify the purpose of the anecdote
Ask yourself: why is this dream mentioned? It serves to demonstrate Ibn Khafif's spiritual rank and his orthodoxy (agreement with al-Ash'ari).
The passage explicitly says it indicates his spiritual rank.
3
Reflect on the phrase 'people of certainty'
Consider what 'ahl al-yaqin' (people of certainty) means. It denotes a high level of faith and spiritual realization.
This phrase is the core of the dream's message.
4
Consider the broader context
Understand that this anecdote is part of a biography that confirms Ibn Khafif's creed aligns with Ash'arism, reinforcing his authority.
The passage mentions the book contains details of his creed in agreement with al-Ash'ari.

This dream indicates Ibn Khafif's high spiritual station, as his reproach was divinely disapproved. The anecdote serves as a testament to Ibn Khafif's piety and certainty.

The Questions of Ibrahim and Musa: Implicit vs Explicit
Anecdote about the shaykh's explanation of Ibrahim and Musa's questions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between the nature of Ibrahim's question about resurrection and Musa's request to see Allah, as explained by the shaykh in this anecdote.

Core Idea
Ibrahim asked implicitly, Musa asked explicitly—both sought understanding.

This lesson presents a biographical anecdote from Imam al-Ash'ari's al-Luma', where a shaykh explains the subtle difference between the questions of Prophet Ibrahim and Prophet Musa. Through this story, we learn how Allah responds to each according to the mode of their request, revealing profound truths about divine attributes and the limits of human inquiry.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the dialogue and the flow of the narrative.
Notice how the shaykh begins by explaining the verse about the birds.
2
Identify the two questions
Locate where the shaykh discusses Ibrahim's question and Musa's question. Mark the key Arabic terms تعريض and تصريح.
These terms are central to the distinction.
3
Understand the response
Reflect on why Allah showed Ibrahim the 'how' of the resurrected birds but not the 'how' of giving life itself. Consider the distinction between attribute (الإحياء) and power (المحيي).
The shaykh explains that giving life is an attribute, not a visible act.
4
Summarize the lesson
Write a one-sentence summary of the key difference between Ibrahim's and Musa's modes of asking.
Use the terms implicit and explicit.

الحق -تعالى- على سؤاله بوَفْقِهِ، وقال له : ﴿فَخُذْ أَرْبَعَةٌ مِّنَ الطَّيْرِ فَصُرْهُنَّ﴾، أي : أن هذه علامة على كيفية الإحياء، حتى تعلم أنني قادر على كل شيء. وآخرُ الآية: ﴿وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ اللَّهَ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ﴾ إِشارة إلى هذه القدرة . وحينما استمع أبو الحسن إلى هذا الكلام، اعترف بفضل الشيخ وقال هذا كلام في غاية الجودة. فقال الشيخ : أُرِيدُ أن استمع إلى كلامك أيضا . فقال أبو الحسن: غدًا . قال الشيخ: وجاءَ في اليوم التالي، فَدَقَّ بابي وأخذني إلى داره، وجاء تلاميذه وتَحَلَّقوا حوله . قلت : سَلْهُم . قال : توجيه السؤال إليهم بدعة . قلت : لماذا [ألا] تناقشهم وتعلمهم؟ قال : إنهم يسألون إنكارا، ويجادلون في الباطل، ولكن ما داموا قد سألوا فقد وجبت عليَّ إجابتهم، وحتى إذا لم يكن السؤال على جَادَّةِ الشرع. قال : وقال أبو الحسن كلاما طويلا، ورأيته في غاية الإحكام . قال : في سؤال إبراهيم عليه السلام رَبِّ أَرِنِي كَيْفَ تُحْيِ الْمَوْتَى. وسؤال موسى - عليه السلامُ - وَرَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنْظُرْ إِلَيْكَ . فقلتُ : نعم . قلنا : إن سؤال إبراهيم هو سؤال . موسى، إلا أن سؤال إبراهيم سؤال متمكِّن، وسؤال موسى سؤال صاحبِ غَلَبَةٍ ،وهيجان، فكان تصريحًا ، وسؤال إبراهيم كان تعريضًا ، وذلك أنه قال: ﴿أَرِنِي كَيْفَ تُحْيِ الْمَوْتَى﴾، فأراه كيفية المحيى ، ولم يره كيفية الإحياء؛ لأن الإحياء صفتُه تعالى، والمحيي قدرته، فأجابه إشارةً كما سأله إشارةً، إلا أنه قال في الآخر وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ اللَّهَ عَزِيزٌ حكيم كلمة فالعزيز المنيع . فقال أبو الحسن : هذا كلام صحيحٌ.
He said: "Know that Allah - exalted - upon his question with his success, and said to him: 'Take four birds and incline them towards you.' That is: this is a sign of the manner of giving life, so that you know that I am capable of everything. And the end of the verse: 'And know that Allah is Mighty, Wise' is an indication of this power." And when Abu al-Hasan heard this speech, he acknowledged the shaykh's merit and said: "This is excellent speech." So the shaykh said: "I want to hear your speech as well." Abu al-Hasan said: "Tomorrow." The shaykh said: "He came the next day, knocked on my door, and took me to his house. His students came and gathered around him. I said: 'Ask them.' He said: 'Directing the question to them is an innovation.' I said: 'Why do you not debate them and teach them?' He said: 'They ask in denial and argue falsely, but since they have asked, it is obligatory upon me to answer them, even if the question is not along the path of the Law.'" He said: "And Abu al-Hasan spoke at length, and I saw it as most precise." He said: "Concerning the question of Ibrahim, peace be upon him: 'My Lord, show me how You give life to the dead.' And the question of Musa, peace be upon him: 'My Lord, show me so that I may look upon You.' I said: 'Yes.' We said: 'Indeed, the question of Ibrahim is the question of Musa, except that the question of Ibrahim is the question of one who is settled, and the question of Musa is the question of one overcome and agitated, so it was explicit, and the question of Ibrahim was implicit. That is because he said: "Show me how You give life to the dead," so He showed him the mode of the one given life, but did not show him the mode of giving life; because giving life is His attribute, and the giver of life is His power. So He answered him by sign just as he asked by sign, except that He said at the end: "And know that Allah is Mighty, Wise" - a word: 'the Mighty, the Invincible.'" Then Abu al-Hasan said: "This is correct speech."
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a biographical anecdote. It begins with a shaykh explaining the meaning of God's command to Ibrahim to take four birds and incline them towards Him, and that the end of the verse indicates God's power. Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari praises the shaykh's speech. The shaykh then asks to hear Abu al-Hasan's speech. The next day, Abu al-Hasan comes to the shaykh's house where students have gathered. Abu al-Hasan suggests the shaykh ask the students questions, but the shaykh refuses, calling it an innovation. When pressed, the shaykh explains that the students ask in denial and argue falsely, yet he is obligated to answer them even if their questions are not in accordance with the Law. The shaykh then addresses the question of Ibrahim and Musa. He says that Ibrahim's request to see how God gives life to the dead and Musa's request to see God are similar, but Ibrahim's is asked with assurance while Musa's is asked out of overwhelming desire, thus it was explicit, whereas Ibrahim's was implicit. God showed Ibrahim the manner of the one given life, not the manner of giving life itself, because giving life is an attribute of God and the act of giving life is His power. God answered by sign as he asked by sign, and the verse ends with 'Know that Allah is Mighty, Wise,' indicating God's might. Abu al-Hasan affirms the correctness of this explanation.

Key Terms
كيفية الإحياء
المحيي
الإحياء
تعريض
تصريح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think both Ibrahim and Musa asked for the same thing; the passage clarifies the difference in their modes of questioning.
Correction: Ibrahim's question was implicit (تعريض) while Musa's was explicit (تصريح), and God responded accordingly.

Checkpoint
According to the shaykh, what is the difference between the question of Ibrahim and the question of Musa?
A) Ibrahim asked explicitly, Musa asked implicitly.
B) Ibrahim's question was implicit, Musa's was explicit.
C) Ibrahim asked about power, Musa asked about vision.
D) Both questions were the same.

Key Takeaway
The mode of asking (implicit vs explicit) influences how Allah responds, but both Ibrahim and Musa sought deeper knowledge of divine power and essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon Allah, do you trust that He knows the best way to answer you—sometimes with a sign rather than a direct fulfillment? Examine your heart: are you like Ibrahim, settled in faith, or like Musa, overwhelmed by emotion? What does your mode of asking reveal about your certainty in Allah's wisdom? Commit today to ask with tamakkun (settledness), trusting that His response, whether implicit or explicit, is perfect.
?
The shaykh felt obligated to answer even those who asked in denial. Think of someone in your life who questions your faith with insincerity. Do you avoid them, or do you engage with patience? How does this anecdote challenge you to teach and clarify even when the asker's intention is flawed? Pray for the strength to respond with knowledge and grace.

The Fourth Student: Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari and the Spread of Ash'arism in Syria
Biographical note on the fourth student of al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari as a student of al-Ash'ari and his contribution to spreading the Ash'ari school in Syria.

Core Idea
The fourth student of al-Ash'ari carried his teachings to Syria.

This lesson introduces us to Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari, the fourth student of Imam al-Ash'ari. Through biographical details, we learn how he not only received knowledge directly from his teacher but also played a key role in disseminating the Ash'ari school in Syria. The passage also highlights his scholarly work and his connections with other scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Focus on identifying who this person is and what he did.
The passage contains a quote from Ibn Asakir.
2
Identify key facts about al-Tabari
List the key facts: he was a student of al-Ash'ari, he was from the Tabari family, he went to Syria, he spread the Ash'ari school, and he wrote a book on principles.
Note the distinction between this al-Tabari and Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari.
3
Reflect on his contribution
Consider how al-Tabari's travel to Syria and teaching helped establish the Ash'ari school outside Iraq. How do such individual efforts shape the spread of a school of thought?
This connects to the broader history of the Ash'ari school.

٤ ورابع التلاميذ : أبو الحسن عبد العزيز بن محمد بن إسحاق الطبري [ما بين ٣٦٠هـ - ٣٧٠هـ] : وممن تلقوا عن أبي الحسن الأشعري - أيضًا - عِلْمَه ومذهبه ، واختلف إليه وصَحِبَه : الطبري أبو الحسن عبد العزيز، فالطبريون كثيرون في الشام وهم على مذهب الأشعرية». تَرْجَمَ له ابنُ عساكر في أخِصَّاء أصحاب أبي الحسن، فقال: كان من أعيان أصحاب أبي الحسن وممن تخرج به، وخرج إلى الشام، ونشر بها مذهبه، وكتب عن أبي جعفر محمد بن جَرِيرٍ الطّبري كتابه في التفسير ، وسَمِعَه منه . ووقفت له قديمًا على تأليف في «الأصول»، يدلُّ على فضل كثير وعلم غزير، سماه : كتاب
4. And the fourth of the students: Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Aziz ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Tabari [between 360 AH - 370 AH]: And among those who received from Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari - also - his knowledge and his school, and attended him and accompanied him: al-Tabari Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Aziz. And the Tabaris are many in al-Sham (Syria) and they are upon the school of the Ash'aris. Ibn Asakir wrote his biography in 'The Close Companions of Abu al-Hasan', saying: He was among the prominent companions of Abu al-Hasan and among those who graduated with him. He went out to al-Sham and spread his school there. He wrote from Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari his book of Tafsir and heard it from him. And I came across earlier a composition of his on 'al-Usul' (Principles), indicating great virtue and abundant knowledge, he named it: Kitab...
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note listing the fourth student of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari: Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Aziz al-Tabari. It states that he was among those who received knowledge and the school (madhhab) from al-Ash'ari, attending him and accompanying him. It notes that the Tabari family is numerous in Syria and they adhere to the Ash'ari school. Ibn Asakir, in his work on the close companions of Abu al-Hasan, wrote that al-Tabari was one of the prominent companions and graduates of al-Ash'ari. He traveled to Syria and spread the Ash'ari school there. He also studied under Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari, writing his Tafsir and hearing it from him. The author mentions having seen an earlier composition by al-Tabari on the 'Principles' (al-Usul), which showed great merit and extensive knowledge, titled 'Kitab' (Book).

Key Terms

الأشعرية
الأصول
الطبري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Confusing Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari with the famous historian and mufassir Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari.
Correction: Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari is a different scholar; he was a student of al-Ash'ari and wrote on principles, while Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari is known for his Tafsir and history.

Checkpoint

D) He was a student of al-Ash'ari but left his school.

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari was a key student of al-Ash'ari who spread the Ash'ari school in Syria and authored works on principles.

?

Two Disciples of Al-Ash'ari: Al-Tabari and Al-Sarakhsi
Biographical sketches of two Ash'ari disciples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identities and contributions of two key disciples of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari: al-Tabari and al-Sarakhsi.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's disciples spread his doctrine across the Islamic world.

This passage introduces two more disciples of al-Ash'ari, highlighting their scholarly achievements and roles in disseminating Ash'ari theology. Al-Tabari was a prolific writer and defender of Sunnism, while al-Sarakhsi hosted al-Ash'ari in his home and was a polymath.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Let the flow of names and accomplishments sink in.
Notice the use of dates and scholarly lineages.
2
Identify the two disciples and their key attributes
For each disciple, note their full name, where they studied, what they wrote, and how they contributed to the Ash'ari school.
Al-Tabari authored a refutation of atheists; al-Sarakhsi was a host to al-Ash'ari.
3
Reflect on their roles in spreading Ash'arism
Consider how al-Tabari's migration to Sham and al-Sarakhsi's hosting of al-Ash'ari directly aided the spread of the doctrine.
Their scholarly output also played a key role.

رابع التلاميذ : أبو الحسن عبد العزيز بن محمد بن إسحاق الطبري [ما بين ٣٦٠هـ - ٣٧٠هـ] : وممن تلقوا عن أبي الحسن الأشعري - أيضًا - عِلْمَه ومذهبه، واختلف إليه وصَحِبَه : الطبري أبو الحسن عبد العزيز، فالطبريون كثيرون في الشام وهم على مذهب الأشعرية. تَرْجَمَ له ابنُ عساكر في أخِصَّاء أصحاب أبي الحسن، فقال: كان من أعيان أصحاب أبي الحسن وممن تخرج به، وخرج إلى الشام، ونشر بها مذهبه، وكتب عن أبي جعفر محمد بن جَرِيرٍ الطّبري كتابه في التفسير، وسَمِعَه منه. ووقفت له قديمًا على تأليف في «الأصول»، يدلُّ على فضل كثير وعلم غزير، سماه : كتاب رياضة المبتدي وبصيرة المستهدِي، وسكن دمشق، ونشر بها مذهب أهل السنة. له تصانيف حسنةٌ منها : «رياضة المبتدي» في الرد على الملاحدة، ومن ضاهاهم من المبتدعة، وكتاب في «الرَّد على جعفر بن حرب، وهو من شيوخ المعتزلة، وفي نقض مسائله». ه - والخامس : أبو علي زاهر بن أحمدَ السَّرخَسِيُّ [٢٩٣هـ - ٣٨٩هـ ] ولا يمكن عند ذكر تلاميذ أبي الحسن، أن نغفل الرجل الذي مات أبو الحسن في داره وحِجْرِه، وذكره ابن عساكر في أصحابه . . . قال نقلا عن الحاكم : «زاهرُ بنُ أحمدَ بن محمد بنِ عيسى السَّرْخَسِيُّ، أبو عليّ، المقرى، الفقيه، المُحَدِّثُ، عصره بخراسان . . . وقد كان قرأ القرآن على أبي بكر بن مجاهد، وتَفَقَّة عند أبي إسحاقَ المَرْوَزِيّ؛ ودرس الأدب على أبي بكر بن الأَنْبَارِيِّ، ومحمد بن يحيى الصُّولِيّ صاحب «أدب الكتاب»، وأقرانهما، فهو متكلّم، محدث، أديب، متفقه. شيخ عَمَّرَ طويلا، وتُوفِّيَ ... يوم الأربعاء سلخ ربيع الآخر، من سنة تسع وثمانين وثلاث مئةٍ، وهو ابنُ ست وتسعين سنةٌ .
The fourth of the disciples: Abu al-Hasan ‘Abd al-‘Aziz ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Tabari [between 360 and 370 AH]. Among those who also received from Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari his knowledge and doctrine, and frequented him and accompanied him: al-Tabari Abu al-Hasan ‘Abd al-‘Aziz. The Tabaris are many in Sham and they follow the Ash‘ari doctrine. Ibn ‘Asakir gave his biography among the close companions of Abu al-Hasan, saying: He was one of the eminent companions of Abu al-Hasan and among those who graduated under him. He went out to Sham and spread his doctrine there. He transcribed from Abu Ja‘far Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari his book of Tafsir and heard it from him. I came across a work of his in usul (principles) indicating great merit and abundant knowledge; he named it: 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi wa Basirat al-Mustahdi'. He resided in Damascus and spread the Sunnite doctrine there. He has excellent writings, among them: 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi' in refutation of the atheists and those who resemble them among the innovators, and a book on the 'Refutation of Ja‘far ibn Harb', who was one of the Mu‘tazilite shaykhs, and on the refutation of his questions. Fifth: Abu ‘Ali Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi [293-389 AH]. It is not possible, when mentioning the disciples of Abu al-Hasan, to overlook the man in whose house and lap Abu al-Hasan died. Ibn ‘Asakir mentioned him among his companions… He said, quoting from al-Hakim: 'Zahir ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn ‘Isa al-Sarakhsi, Abu ‘Ali, the Quran reciter, the jurist, the hadith scholar, the unique of his age in Khurasan… He had read the Quran to Abu Bakr ibn Mujahid, and studied fiqh under Abu Ishaq al-Marwazi, and studied adab under Abu Bakr al-Anbari and Muhammad ibn Yahya al-Suli, author of 'Adab al-Kuttab', and their peers. So he is a mutakallim, muhaddith, adib, and faqih. He lived a long life and died… on Wednesday, the end of Rabi‘ al-Akhir of the year 389 AH, at the age of ninety-six years.'
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage provides brief biographies of the fourth and fifth disciples of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari. The fourth is Abu al-Hasan ‘Abd al-‘Aziz al-Tabari, whose active years are given as between 360 and 370 AH. The text notes that the Tabari family is numerous in the Levant (Sham) and all follow the Ash‘ari school. Ibn ‘Asakir recorded that he was among the most prominent of al-Ash‘ari's companions and that he studied under him, then traveled to Sham and propagated his master's doctrine. He also studied under the famous mufassir Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari, copying his Tafsir. The passage mentions that the author found a work by al-Tabari in usul (principles of religion) titled 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi wa Basirat al-Mustahdi', indicating his scholarly depth. He lived in Damascus and authored works defending the Sunni creed against atheists and heretics, including a refutation of the Mu‘tazilite Ja‘far ibn Harb. The fifth disciple is Abu ‘Ali Zahir al-Sarakhsi, notable for being the host in whose house al-Ash‘ari passed away. The passage quotes al-Hakim to describe his scholarly profile: he was a Quran reciter, jurist, hadith scholar, and adib (literary scholar). He studied under many leading scholars of the time: Quran from Abu Bakr ibn Mujahid, fiqh from Abu Ishaq al-Marwazi, and adab from Abu Bakr al-Anbari and Muhammad ibn Yahya al-Suli. Thus he combined multiple disciplines: kalam, hadith, adab, and fiqh. He lived to an old age, dying at 96 in the year 389 AH.

Key Terms

أصحاب
طبري
سرخسي
أشعري
رياضة المبتدي
رد على الملاحدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think al-Sarakhsi was a student of Ibn Jarir al-Tabari.
Correction: Actually, it was al-Tabari (the disciple) who studied under Ibn Jarir al-Tabari, not al-Sarakhsi.

Checkpoint

B) He was a student of Ibn Jarir al-Tabari.
C) He was a disciple of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and died in his house.
D) He wrote a book called 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi'.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's disciples actively spread his teachings through writing, teaching, and hosting, ensuring the survival of his school.

A host for his teacher and a scholar of many sciences.

Among al-Ash'ari's students, one man stands out for the privilege of hosting the Imam in his final days. Abu Ali Zahir al-Sarkhasi was a renowned scholar in Quran, jurisprudence, hadith, and literature. This lesson introduces his biography and his unique connection to al-Ash'ari.

ه - والخامس : أبو علي زاهر بن أحمدَ السَّرخَسِيُّ [٢٩٣هـ - ٣٨٩هـ ] ولا يمكن عند ذكر تلاميذ أبي الحسن، أن نغفل الرجل الذي مات أبو الحسن في داره وحِجْرِه، وذكره ابن عساكر» في أصحابه . . . قال نقلا عن الحاكم : «زاهرُ بنُ أحمدَ بن محمد بنِ - عيسى السَّرْخَسِيُّ ، أبو عليّ، المقرى، الفقيه، المُحَدِّثُ، عصره بخراسان . . . وقد كان قرأ القرآن على أبي بكر بن مجاهد، وتَفَقَّة عند أبي إسحاقَ المَرْوَزِيّ ; ودرس الأدب على أبي بكر بن الأَنْبَارِيِّ، ومحمد بن يحيى الصُّولِيّ صاحب «أدب الكتاب»، وأقرانهما ، فهو متكلّم، محدث، أديب، متفقه . شیخ عَمَّرَ طويلا ، وتُوفِّيَ ... يوم الأربعاء سلخ ربيع الآخر، من سنة تسع وثمانين وثلاث مئةٍ، وهو ابنُ ست وتسعين سنةٌ . . (۲) . ورَوَى ابن عساكر، عن أبي حازم عمر بن الحافظ قال : سمعت أبا علي زاهر بن أحمد السرخسي يقول : «لما قرب حضور أجل أبي الحسن الأشعري -رحمه الله - في داري ببغداد، دعاني فأتيته . قال اشهد علي أنني لا أُكَفِّر أحدًا من أهل هذه القبلة ; لأن الكل يشيرون إلى معبود واحد ، وإنما هذا كله اختلاف العبارات (۱). ونقل ابن عساكر أيضًا عن ابن فورك أن السَّرْخَسِيَّ كان من أصحاب الشيخ أبي الحسن ببغداد (۲) .
5 - And the fifth: Abu Ali Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Sarkhasi (293-389 AH). It is not possible when mentioning the students of Abu al-Hasan to overlook the man in whose house and care Abu al-Hasan died, and Ibn Asakir mentioned him among his companions . . . He said, quoting from al-Hakim: Zahir ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Isa al-Sarkhasi, Abu Ali, the reciter, the jurist, the hadith scholar, his era in Khurasan . . . He studied the Quran under Abu Bakr ibn Mujahid, and studied jurisprudence under Abu Ishaq al-Marwazi; and studied literature under Abu Bakr al-Anbari and Muhammad ibn Yahya al-Suli, author of Adab al-Kitab, and their peers. He was a theologian, hadith scholar, literary scholar, and jurist. He lived long and died . . . on Wednesday, the last day of Rabi' al-Akhir, in the year 389 AH, being ninety-six years old . . . (2). And Ibn Asakir narrated, from Abu Hazim Umar ibn al-Hafiz, who said: I heard Abu Ali Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Sarkhasi say: When the time of the death of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari - may Allah have mercy on him - drew near in my house in Baghdad, he called me and I came. He said: Bear witness concerning me that I do not declare any of the people of this qibla as disbelievers; because all of them point to one object of worship, and this is only a difference of expressions (1). And Ibn Asakir also transmitted from Ibn Furak that al-Sarkhasi was among the companions of the Shaykh Abu al-Hasan in Baghdad (2).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This is a biographical passage about a fifth student of al-Ash'ari, Abu Ali Zahir al-Sarkhasi. The passage begins by explaining his importance: he hosted al-Ash'ari in his own house and was present at his death. The author then gives his full name and describes his scholarly background: he studied Quran, jurisprudence, literature under famous teachers, and was proficient in theology, hadith, literature, and fiqh. It then records his date of death (389 AH at age 96). The most significant part follows: a narration from al-Sarkhasi himself about al-Ash'ari's deathbed statement. Al-Ash'ari called him and asked him to bear witness that he (al-Ash'ari) does not declare any of the people of the qibla (i.e., Muslims who pray towards Mecca) as disbelievers (kafirs). The reason given is that all of them point to one object of worship, and their differences are only in expressions (ikhtilaf al-'ibarat). This is a key statement in al-Ash'ari's stance on avoiding takfir of other Muslims despite doctrinal disagreements. Finally, the passage notes that Ibn Furak confirmed al-Sarkhasi's close association with al-Ash'ari in Baghdad.

المتفقه

Al-Ash'ari's Deathbed Statement on Takfir
Al-Ash'ari's deathbed testimony forbidding takfir of Ahl al-Qibla and attributing differences to variance in expression.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's deathbed declaration regarding not declaring Muslims disbelievers and the principle of ikhtilaf al-'ibarat (difference of expressions).

Core Idea
Differences in expression do not justify takfir.

On his deathbed, Imam al-Ash'ari gave a final testament that would define his school's stance on religious disagreements. He explicitly forbade takfir of Ahl al-Qibla, arguing that all Muslims worship the same God. This lesson examines that statement.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ash'ari's deathbed statement
Read the Arabic passage where al-Ash'ari calls al-Sarkhasi and makes his declaration. Read the translation carefully.
Note the wording: 'I do not declare any of the people of this qibla as disbelievers'.
2
Understand the reason given
Al-Ash'ari gives a reason: 'because all of them point to one object of worship'. This is a theological principle.
The unity of the object of worship is the basis for unity.
3
Analyze the phrase 'ikhtilaf al-'ibarat'
Al-Ash'ari says the differences among Muslims are only a difference of expressions. This means that doctrinal disagreements do not change the fundamental belief in one God.
This is a key Ash'ari stance on theological diversity.

Source Text

C) He said only his own followers are saved.
D) He said only the Mu'tazila are disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's deathbed declaration establishes the principle of not declaring fellow Muslims disbelievers due to theological differences, attributing them to variance in expression.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Think of a specific theological disagreement you have with another Muslim. Is it really a difference in what they worship, or only a difference in how they express it? Are you willing to treat it as mere expression—and if not, what is holding you back?
?
Al-Ash'ari chose to utter this testimony on his deathbed. What does that tell you about the urgency of guarding unity among Ahl al-Qibla? Is there any pride in your own school that you need to abandon before you meet Allah?

Bandar al-Shirazi: The Servant of al-Ash'ari
Introduction of Bandar al-Shirazi as a close companion of al-Ash'ari, known for his knowledge of principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the close personal and scholarly relationship between Abu al-Husayn Bandar al-Shirazi and Imam al-Ash'ari, and how he exemplified the Ash'ari ethos of avoiding takfir.

Core Idea
Bandar al-Shirazi was both a mystic and a scholar of usul, known as the servant of al-Ash'ari.

This lesson introduces one of the most intimate companions of Imam al-Ash'ari: Abu al-Husayn Bandar al-Shirazi. He was a mystic (mutasawwif) and a scholar of principles, known as the 'servant of Abu al-Hasan.' His biography highlights the diversity of al-Ash'ari's students and the core principle of refraining from declaring fellow Muslims disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the key phrases: 'khadim Abi al-Hasan' and 'alimun bil-usul'.
Pay attention to the comparison with Zahir al-Sarkhasi.
2
Understand Bandar's role
Bandar was a close servant and student. Consider what 'khadim' implies about his relationship with al-Ash'ari.
3
Note the takfir principle
The passage includes al-Ash'ari's dying words: 'I do not declare anyone of the people of this qibla as a disbeliever.' Reflect on its significance.
This was a key stance of al-Ash'ari.
4
Appreciate the scholarly context
Bandar was a scholar of usul and had 'the well-known tongue', indicating eloquence. How does this fit with being a mystic?
This shows the breadth of al-Ash'ari's circle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا نستطيع أن تُنهي الكلام عن أخِصَّاء أبي الحسن من تلامذته، دون أن نذكر أبا الحسين بندارَ بن الحسين الشيرازي، المتصوف كابن خفيف وَبلَدِيَّه ، (ت : ٣٥٣هـ)، وقد عرف بأنه خادم أبي الحسن»؛ فهو ينافس زاهرًا السرْخَسِيَّ، في صلته الحميمة بالشيخ - رضي الله عنه ، وما قدمت السَّرخَسِيَّ إلا لإيوائه الشيخ في بيته، حيث أسلم روحه لباريها، دون زوجة أو ولد، وهو يردد : إني لا أكفُرُ أحدا من أهل هذه القبلة . هذا، وقد قال السُّلمي في الطبقات (۳) عن بُندارَ : من أهل شیراز، سَكَن أرَّجان، وكان عالما بالأصول، له اللسان المشهود
And we cannot end the speech about the close associates of Abu al-Hasan from his students without mentioning Abu al-Husayn Bandar ibn al-Husayn al-Shirazi, the mystic like Ibn Khafif and his countryman, (d. 353 AH), and he was known as the servant of Abu al-Hasan; so he rivals Zahir al-Sarkhasi in his intimate connection with the Shaykh - may Allah be pleased with him. And I have only mentioned al-Sarkhasi before him because he gave shelter to the Shaykh in his house, where he surrendered his soul to its Creator, without wife or child, while saying repeatedly: I do not declare anyone of the people of this qibla as a disbeliever. And al-Sulami said in the Tabaqat (3) about Bandar: from the people of Shiraz, he lived in Arrajan, and he was a scholar of principles (usul), having the well-known tongue.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage introduces another prominent student of al-Ash'ari: Abu al-Husayn Bandar al-Shirazi. It describes him as a mystic (mutasawwif) like Ibn Khafif, and notes that he was known as the 'servant of Abu al-Hasan' (khadim Abi al-Hasan), indicating his close personal service to al-Ash'ari. The author compares his closeness to that of Zahir al-Sarkhasi, but explains that he mentioned al-Sarkhasi first because al-Sarkhasi hosted al-Ash'ari in his home during his final moments. The passage also echoes the theme of refraining from takfir: al-Ash'ari died repeating 'I do not declare anyone of the people of this qibla as a disbeliever.' Finally, the author quotes al-Sulami's Tabaqat al-Sufiyya, stating that Bandar was from Shiraz, lived in Arrajan, was a scholar of usul (foundational principles of religion), and was renowned for his eloquent speech.

Misconception: Some might think al-Ash'ari's students were only theologians, but this shows they also included mystics and scholars of usul.
Correction: Bandar al-Shirazi was a mystic (mutasawwif) and a scholar of usul, demonstrating the diversity of al-Ash'ari's students.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Is there any person or group you are tempted to declare outside the fold of Islam? How can you train your heart to refrain from takfir, especially toward those who follow the same qibla?

Al-Ash'ari's Final Words on Ahl al-Qibla
Ibn 'Asakir narrates al-Ash'ari's deathbed statement and notes al-Sarakhsi's discipleship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's deathbed stance on not excommunicating Ahl al-Qibla and its basis in the unity of the object of worship.

Core Idea
Differences among Muslims are only in expressions, not in object of worship.

This lesson presents a famous report from Ibn 'Asakir about Imam al-Ash'ari's final words. On his deathbed, he made a clear declaration about not excommunicating fellow Muslims who pray towards the same qibla. This statement encapsulates his approach to theological disagreements within the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Pay attention to the context: it is a deathbed statement witnessed by al-Sarakhsi.
Notice that the report comes through two chains: through al-Sarakhsi and through Ibn Furak.
2
Identify the core claim
Al-Ash'ari says he does not excommunicate (yukaffir) anyone from Ahl al-Qibla. What is the scope of this claim?
It is specifically about those who face the qibla in prayer, i.e., Muslims.
3
Understand the reasoning
The reason given is that all Ahl al-Qibla point to one object of worship (ma'būd wāḥid). Differences are only in expressions (ikhtilāf al-ʿibārāt).
This implies that as long as the object of worship is the same, verbal differences do not warrant excommunication.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why a dying scholar would make this statement. It shows his deep concern for unity and avoiding takfir based on theological disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى ابن عساكر، عن أبي حازم عمر بن الحافظ قال : سمعت أبا علي زاهر بن أحمد السرخسي يقول : «لما قرب حضور أجل أبي الحسن الأشعري -رحمه الله - في داري ببغداد، دعاني فأتيته . قال اشهد علي أنني لا أُكَفِّر أحدًا من أهل هذه القبلة ؛ لأن الكل يشيرون إلى معبود واحد ، وإنما هذا كله اختلاف العبارات (۱).
ونقل ابن عساكر أيضًا عن ابن فورك أن السَّرْخَسِيَّ كان من أصحاب الشيخ أبي الحسن ببغداد (۲) .
Ibn ʿAsākir narrated, from Abū Ḥāzim ʿUmar ibn al-Ḥāfiẓ, who said: I heard Abū ʿAlī Zāhir ibn Aḥmad al-Sarakhsī saying: 'When the time of the death of Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī (may Allah have mercy on him) drew near in my house in Baghdad, he called me and I came to him. He said: Bear witness against me that I do not excommunicate anyone from the people of this qibla; because all of them point to one object of worship, and this is all merely a difference of expressions (1).' And Ibn ʿAsākir also transmitted from Ibn Fūrak that al-Sarakhsī was among the companions of Shaykh Abī al-Ḥasan in Baghdad (2).
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage transmits two related reports from Ibn ʿAsākir about Imam al-Ashʿarī's final days and his student Zāhir al-Sarakhsī. The first report, via Abū Ḥāzim from al-Sarakhsī, recounts al-Ashʿarī's deathbed declaration: he insists that he does not excommunicate (yukaffir) anyone from Ahl al-Qibla (the people of the qibla, i.e., Muslims who pray towards Mecca). The reason he gives is that all of them point to one object of worship (maʿbūd wāḥid), and differences are only in expressions (ikhtilāf al-ʿibārāt). This is a foundational statement of al-Ashʿarī's stance on takfīr—avoiding hasty excommunication of fellow Muslims who affirm tawḥīd. The second report, directly from Ibn Fūrak, confirms that al-Sarakhsī was a close companion (aṣḥāb) of al-Ashʿarī in Baghdad, emphasizing his role as a trusted student and transmitter.

Key Terms
إكفار
أهل القبلة
اختلاف العبارات
زاهر السرخسي
ابن عساكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari's statement is sometimes misinterpreted as denying excommunication in all cases, even for those who reject fundamental beliefs.
Correction: He specifically limits it to Ahl al-Qibla who affirm the same object of worship. Differences in expressions do not warrant takfir, but core denials of tawhid might.

Checkpoint
Why did Imam al-Ashʿarī say he does not excommunicate anyone from Ahl al-Qibla?
A) Because all Muslims are infallible.
B) Because they all point to one object of worship, and differences are only in expressions.
C) Because excommunication is forbidden in Islam.
D) Because he doubted his own faith.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's deathbed statement emphasizes that as long as Muslims affirm the same object of worship, differences in expressions do not justify excommunication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disagree with another Muslim on a matter of religion, do you ever find yourself harboring inward disdain or suspicion of their faith? What does al-Ash'ari's deathbed declaration reveal about the danger of that attitude?
?
Is there any Muslim group or individual you have mentally 'excommunicated' from your heart? What would it take for you to extend the same grace to them that al-Ash'ari extended on his deathbed?
?
Al-Ash'ari said differences are only in 'expressions'. Reflect on a theological disagreement you have with another Muslim. Is it truly just a difference in expression, or does it touch on the object of worship itself? How can you ensure your heart remains linked to the same maʿbūd wāḥid while disagreeing on wording?

Bundār al-Shīrāzī: A Devoted Servant of al-Ashʿarī
Editor introduces Bundār al-Shīrāzī and quotes al-Sulamī's praise and closing poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of Bundār al-Shīrāzī as a devoted student of Imam al-Ashʿarī and the historical testimonies to his scholarly and spiritual stature.

Core Idea
Bundār al-Shīrāzī was a devoted servant of al-Ashʿarī, honored by mystics and scholars alike.

In this biographical sketch, the editor turns to another close associate of Imam al-Ashʿarī: Abū al-Ḥusayn Bundār al-Shīrāzī. The passage highlights Bundār's unique epithet as 'the servant of Abū al-Ḥasan' and records the praise of the renowned mystic al-Sulamī. It also includes a poetic reflection that concludes the discussion of al-Ashʿarī's life. Through this, we see the deep personal bonds and spiritual legacy among al-Ashʿarī's students.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography of Bundār
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of Bundār's life and his relationship with al-Ashʿarī.
Pay attention to the epithet 'khādim Abī al-Ḥasan'.
2
Understand the comparison with al-Sarakhsī
The editor contrasts Bundār with Zāhir al-Sarakhsī, who was given precedence because he hosted al-Ashʿarī at death. Consider what this tells us about the priority of service.
Al-Sarakhsī's sheltering led to al-Ashʿarī's final moments.
3
Examine al-Sulamī's testimony
Read al-Sulamī's description of Bundār as a scholar of uṣūl and a master of 'ilm al-ḥaqā’iq', honored by al-Shiblī and a discussant with Ibn Khafīf.
'Uṣūl' here likely refers to uṣūl al-dīn (theology).
4
Reflect on the closing poetry
The three lines of poetry speak of being disciplined by time and sharing both hardship and ease. Consider how this fits the theme of a scholar's life.
Poetry is attributed to Bundār by al-Sulamī.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا نستطيع أن ننهي الكلام عن أخِصَّاء أبي الحسن من تلامذته، دون أن نذكر أبا الحسين بندارَ بن الحسين الشيرازي، المتصوف كابن خفيف وَبلَدِيَّه ، (ت : ٣٥٣هـ)، وقد عرف بأنه خادم أبي الحسن»؛ فهو ينافس زاهرًا السَّرْخَسِيَّ، في صلته الحميمة بالشيخ - رضي الله عنه، وما قدمت السَّرْخَسِيَّ إلا لإيوائه الشيخ في بيته، حيث أسلم روحه لباريها، دون زوجة أو ولد، وهو يردد : إني لا أكفُرُ أحدا من أهل هذه القبلة . هذا، وقد قال السُّلمي في الطبقات (۳) عن بُندارَ : من أهل ،شیراز، سَكَن أرَّجان، وكان عالما بالأصول، له اللسان المشهود في علم الحقائق، وكان أبو بكر الشَّبلي يكرمُهُ ، ويُعظَّم قدره، وبينه وبين أبي عبد الله ابن خفيف مُفاوضات في مسائل شتّى». ثم روى عددًا من أقواله النفيسة في السلوك والمعرفة ختمها بأبيات ثلاثة رقيقة نختم بها الكلام عن حياة أبي الحسن ومسيرته الفكرية : نوائب الدهر أدَّبَتني وإِنَّما يُوعَظُ الأريبُ قد ذُقتُ حُلْوًا وذقت مرا كذاك عيش الفتى ضُروب ما مر بُؤْس ولا نعيمُ إِلَّا ولي منهما نَصيبُ(۱)
And we cannot conclude the discussion about the close associates of Abū al-Ḥasan from his students, without mentioning Abū al-Ḥusayn Bundār ibn al-Ḥusayn al-Shīrāzī, the mystic like Ibn Khafīf and his fellow countryman, (d. 353 AH), who was known as 'the servant of Abū al-Ḥasan'; so he rivals Zāhir al-Sarakhsī in his intimate connection with the Shaykh (may Allah be pleased with him). And I only gave precedence to al-Sarakhsī because he sheltered the Shaykh in his house, where he surrendered his soul to its Creator, without a wife or child, while repeating: 'I do not excommunicate anyone from the people of this qibla.' Now, al-Sulamī said in al-Ṭabaqāt (3) about Bundār: 'From the people of Shiraz, he resided in Arrajān, and he was a scholar of uṣūl (foundations), possessing a renowned tongue in the science of realities, and Abū Bakr al-Shiblī honored him and magnified his status, and between him and Abū ʿAbd Allāh ibn Khafīf there were discussions on various matters.' Then he narrated a number of his precious sayings in conduct and knowledge, concluding with three delicate lines of poetry with which we conclude the discussion on the life of Abū al-Ḥasan and his intellectual journey: 'The calamities of time have disciplined me, and only the intelligent are admonished. I have tasted sweet and tasted bitter; thus the life of a youth has various ways. No hardship nor ease has passed except that I have a share from both.' (1)
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Bundār al-Shīrāzī by the editor. It begins by stating that Bundār must be mentioned among the close students of al-Ashʿarī. Bundār is described as a mystic (mutaṣawwif) like Ibn Khafīf and his fellow countryman. He died in 353 AH and was known as 'the servant of Abū al-Ḥasan' (khādim Abī al-Ḥasan). The editor notes that Bundār rivals Zāhir al-Sarakhsī in his intimate connection to al-Ashʿarī, but al-Sarakhsī was given precedence because he hosted al-Ashʿarī in his house at the time of his death, during which al-Ashʿarī repeated his famous statement about not excommunicating Ahl al-Qibla. The editor then quotes al-Sulamī's entry on Bundār from his Ṭabaqāt al-Ṣūfiyya: Bundār was from Shiraz, lived in Arrajān, was a scholar of uṣūl (principles, likely meaning uṣūl al-dīn), had a renowned tongue (i.e., eloquent discourse) in the science of realities (ʿilm al-ḥaqāʾiq, a term for deep spiritual knowledge). He was honored by Abū Bakr al-Shiblī, and he held discussions with Ibn Khafīf on various matters. Al-Sulamī then transmitted precious sayings of Bundār on spiritual conduct and knowledge, which he concluded with three lines of poetry. The editor includes these lines as a closing reflection on the life of al-Ashʿarī, though the poetry is likely Bundār's or from another source. The poetry speaks about being disciplined by life's calamities, tasting both sweet and bitter, and having a share of every experience.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Bundār is often considered less significant than Zāhir al-Sarakhsī.
Correction: The passage shows that Bundār was a major student and mystic, recognized by al-Sulamī, honored by al-Shiblī, and engaged in discussions with Ibn Khafīf. His epithet 'khādim Abī al-Ḥasan' and the praise indicate his high stature.

Key Takeaway
Bundār al-Shīrāzī, known as the servant of al-Ashʿarī, was a revered mystic and theologian whose spiritual stature was acknowledged by leading contemporaries.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Bundār was called 'the servant of Abū al-Ḥasan' – a title of honor through humility. Are you willing to serve someone else's legacy, even if it means your own name is remembered only as a servant? Identify one person (a scholar, parent, or mentor) whose knowledge or character you can actively serve this week, and commit to one concrete act of service.
?
The poetry says, 'The calamities of time have disciplined me.' When was a time you were disciplined by hardship but resisted learning from it? Take a current difficulty you are facing and ask yourself: 'If this is a teacher from Allah, what lesson is it trying to teach me?' Write it down and make a plan to apply that lesson.
?
Bundār tasted both sweet and bitter, and had a share of each. Are you trying to control your life to only taste sweetness, avoiding the bitter altogether? Reflect on one bitter experience that you have never thanked Allah for. This week, when you pray, thank Him specifically for that hardship and ask Him to show you its hidden benefit.

Biographical Tribute to Imam al-Ash'ari
Editor narrates praise of al-Ash'ari and cites his poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari's contemporaries honored him and how his life of both ease and hardship shaped his intellectual journey, as captured in his own poetry.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's life mixed sweetness and bitterness, and he learned from both.

This lesson presents a brief biographical tribute from the editor of al-Luma'. It highlights the respect al-Ash'ari received from notable figures such as Abu Bakr al-Shibli and Abu Abdullah ibn Khafif, and concludes with al-Ash'ari's own poetic reflection on a life shaped by both joy and sorrow. This passage offers a human glimpse into the great theologian's character.

Al-Ash'ari as Author and the Sunni Creedal Synthesis
Describes al-Ash'ari's role as author and the Sunni synthesis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as an author who formulated the rational and theological system for the Sunni school, and the intellectual context of his mission.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari built a rational system that united the Sunni community against theological distortions.

In this opening passage, the author introduces Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as more than a mere author—he was the architect of a new rational framework for Sunni Islam. We learn that his work was not a personal project but a synthesis representing the diverse Sunni milieu, from hadith scholars to moderate Hanbalis. This lesson covers his role and the broader Sunni context he aimed to defend.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Ash'ari's self-conception
Read the passage to see that al-Ash'ari saw himself as laying a new intellectual foundation, not creating a personal school.
2
Identify the Sunni groups represented
List the groups mentioned: hadith scholars, Qur'an reciters, Sufis, moderate Hanbalis, followers of the four schools.
3
Recognize the purpose of his work
He aimed to complete the creedal aspect of the Sunni school in defense against distortions from Mu'tazilism and extremism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أ- أبو الحسن الأشعري مؤلفًا : كان إمامنا -رضي الله عنه- مؤلفًا، وصاحب قلم. وكان يُدرِك كما يشعر كلُّ من يقرؤه - أنه يضع أساس بناء عقليّ جديد، ليس مذهبًا لنفسه، أو نزعةً فكرية ذاتية : بل هو الصياغة العقلية، والصناعة الكلامية والنسق الفكري لموقف أو إن شئت لمذهب أهل السنة والجماعة؛ من المحدثين والقراء، وصوفية السلوك والاستقامة، ومعتدلي الحنابلة، وغيرهم من أتباع المذاهب الأربعة التي سادت الوسط السني، وتلقَّتْها الأمة بالقبول في المجال الفقهي العملي، وجاء هو ليكمل البناء، لهذا الموقف - أو المذهب السني – من الجانب الاعتقادي ؛ انتصارًا لأحكام الكتاب والسنة ، التي شوشت عليها نزعاتُ الاعتزال والغلو، والخروج عن الجماعة ،والتشيع بالرغم من جهود الإمام أبي حنيفة النعمان (١٥٠هـ) صاحب الفقه الأكبر ورسالة العالم والمتعلم وغيرهما؛ بحيث يعتبره بعض الباحثين واضع علم الكلام، لكن جهوده بقيت مؤثرة في المجال الحنفي خاصة، وما قام به الشافعي وأحمد رضي الله عنهما- في مقاومة المبتدعين . وقد فعل الأشعري ذلك، لما انقدح في ذهنِهِ، واستقر في قلبه خلال تطور فكري طويل المدى، لا كما تصوّره الحكايات الرمزية ، من الرؤى المنامية والاعتكاف والخلوة لأسبوعين أو ثلاثة، ثم يخرج على الناس بمؤلفات جديدة، وموقف فكري متسق ومتكامل ، وهو المفكر المعروف خلال أعوام، بل عقود، سابقة في الوسط الاعتزالي ؛ مرتبطا بأكبر دعاته حينئذ، وهو الجبائي الكبير، محمد ابن عبد الوهاب - نقول : لقد انقدح في ذهنه، واستقر في وعيه، في منتصف العقد الأخير من القرن الثالث الهجري، وقد قارب عمره الأربعين - أمران : الأمر الأول: استحسان الخوض في علم كلام سُنّي جديد؛ فأصدر كتابه بهذا العنوان الذي يتطابق محتواه مع كتابه الآخر المقطوع بنسبته إليه، وهو : الحث على البحث، وليس كتاب الاستحسان إلا صياغة
A- Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as an author: Our Imam - may Allah be pleased with him - was an author and a writer. He realized, as anyone who reads him feels, that he was laying the foundation of a new intellectual structure, not a personal school or a subjective intellectual tendency, but rather the rational formulation, the theological craft, and the intellectual system for the position - or if you will, the school - of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah: from the hadith scholars and Qur'an reciters, the Sufis of conduct and uprightness, the moderate Hanbalis, and others from the followers of the four schools that prevailed in the Sunni milieu and were accepted by the ummah in the practical jurisprudential field. He came to complete the building of this position - or the Sunni school - from the creedal side, in support of the rulings of the Book and the Sunnah, which had been disturbed by the tendencies of Mu'tazilism, extremism, dissension from the community, and Shi'ism, despite the efforts of Imam Abu Hanifah al-Nu'man (150 AH), the author of al-Fiqh al-Akbar and Risalah al-'Alim wa al-Muta'allim and others, such that some researchers consider him the founder of 'ilm al-kalam, but his efforts remained influential in the Hanafi field especially, and what al-Shafi'i and Ahmad - may Allah be pleased with them - did in resisting the innovators. And al-Ash'ari did that, because there became clear in his mind and settled in his heart during a long-term intellectual development - not as the symbolic stories imagine, from dream visions and seclusion for two or three weeks, then he emerges to people with new works and a consistent and integrated intellectual position, while he was a known thinker for years, rather decades, previously in the Mu'tazili milieu, associated with its greatest caller at that time, al-Jubba'i the elder, Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahhab - we say: there became clear in his mind and settled in his consciousness, in the middle of the last decade of the third century AH, when he was approaching forty, two matters: The first matter: approval of engaging in a new Sunni 'ilm al-kalam; so he issued a book with this title whose content matches his other book whose attribution to him is certain, which is: al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth, and the book al-Istihsan is nothing but a formulation
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological introduction discussing Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's role as an author and the intellectual context behind his work. It begins by affirming that al-Ash'ari was indeed an author and a writer, and that readers can perceive that he was laying the foundation of a new rational structure. This structure was not a personal or subjective school, but rather the rational formulation, theological craft, and intellectual system of the Sunni position, representing various groups: hadith scholars, Qur'an reciters, Sufis, moderate Hanbalis, and followers of the four legal schools. Al-Ash'ari came to complete the creedal aspect of this Sunni position in defense of the Qur'an and Sunnah against distortions from Mu'tazilism, extremism, sectarianism, and Shi'ism. The passage notes that earlier efforts by Abu Hanifah (considered by some the founder of kalam) were influential mainly in Hanafi circles, and that al-Shafi'i and Ahmad also fought innovators. Then it explains that al-Ash'ari's change was the result of a long intellectual development, not sudden dreams or retreats. He had been a known figure in the Mu'tazili school for decades, associated with al-Jubba'i. In his late thirties (around 290 AH), two matters became clear to him: first, the approval of engaging in a new Sunni kalam, leading him to write a book titled 'al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth' (Encouragement of Inquiry), and that the book 'al-Istihsan' is essentially a formulation of that encouragement.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's authorship was a collective effort to articulate the Sunni creed rationally, building on earlier legal foundations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content to passively inherit your creed, or do you actively engage with it as a rational system that requires your personal understanding and defense, as al-Ash'ari did?
?
In what ways do you allow personal preferences or intellectual trends to shape your understanding of Islam, rather than submitting to the collective Sunni tradition that al-Ash'ari worked to articulate?
?
Do you see yourself as a builder of the Sunni synthesis in your own context, or do you neglect the intellectual dimension of faith, leaving the defense of orthodoxy to others?

Al-Ash'ari's Intellectual Journey and the Call to Sunni Kalam
Explains al-Ash'ari's intellectual development and the two matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the long intellectual development that led al-Ash'ari to adopt Sunni kalam, and the two key matters that emerged in his thinking.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's turn to Sunni kalam was a gradual intellectual process, not a sudden conversion.

The passage continues by explaining that al-Ash'ari's shift was the result of a long-term intellectual evolution, contrary to popular symbolic stories. It reveals that in his late thirties, two matters became clear to him: the approval of engaging in a new Sunni kalam, and the publication of a book encouraging inquiry. This lesson examines that development.

Guided Path
1
Reject symbolic stories
Notice how the passage dismisses dream visions and short retreats as explanations for al-Ash'ari's change.
2
Identify the two matters
Find the two matters that became clear to al-Ash'ari: approval of Sunni kalam and the book encouraging inquiry.
3
Connect the books
Understand that al-Istihsan and al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth are essentially the same content.

أ- أبو الحسن الأشعري مؤلفًا : كان إمامنا -رضي الله عنه- مؤلفًا، وصاحب قلم. وكان يُدرِك كما يشعر كلُّ من يقرؤه - أنه يضع أساس بناء عقليّ جديد، ليس مذهبًا لنفسه، أو نزعةً فكرية ذاتية : بل هو الصياغة العقلية، والصناعة الكلامية والنسق الفكري لموقف أو إن شئت لمذهب أهل السنة والجماعة؛ من المحدثين والقراء، وصوفية السلوك والاستقامة، ومعتدلي الحنابلة، وغيرهم من أتباع المذاهب الأربعة التي سادت الوسط السني، وتلقَّتْها الأمة بالقبول في المجال الفقهي العملي، وجاء هو ليكمل البناء، لهذا الموقف - أو المذهب السني – من الجانب الاعتقادي ؛ انتصارًا لأحكام الكتاب والسنة ، التي شوشت عليها نزعاتُ الاعتزال والغلو، والخروج عن الجماعة ،والتشيع بالرغم من جهود الإمام أبي حنيفة النعمان (١٥٠هـ) صاحب الفقه الأكبر ورسالة العالم والمتعلم وغيرهما؛ بحيث يعتبره بعض الباحثين واضع علم الكلام، لكن جهوده بقيت مؤثرة في المجال الحنفي خاصة، وما قام به الشافعي وأحمد رضي الله عنهما- في مقاومة المبتدعين . وقد فعل الأشعري ذلك، لما انقدح في ذهنِهِ، واستقر في قلبه خلال تطور فكري طويل المدى، لا كما تصوّره الحكايات الرمزية ، من الرؤى المنامية والاعتكاف والخلوة لأسبوعين أو ثلاثة، ثم يخرج على الناس بمؤلفات جديدة، وموقف فكري متسق ومتكامل ، وهو المفكر المعروف خلال أعوام، بل عقود، سابقة في الوسط الاعتزالي ؛ مرتبطا بأكبر دعاته حينئذ، وهو الجبائي الكبير، محمد ابن عبد الوهاب - نقول : لقد انقدح في ذهنه، واستقر في وعيه، في منتصف العقد الأخير من القرن الثالث الهجري، وقد قارب عمره الأربعين - أمران : الأمر الأول: استحسان الخوض في علم كلام سُنّي جديد؛ فأصدر كتابه بهذا العنوان الذي يتطابق محتواه مع كتابه الآخر المقطوع بنسبته إليه، وهو : الحث على البحث، وليس كتاب الاستحسان إلا صياغة
A- Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as an author: Our Imam - may Allah be pleased with him - was an author and a writer. He realized, as anyone who reads him feels, that he was laying the foundation of a new intellectual structure, not a personal school or a subjective intellectual tendency, but rather the rational formulation, the theological craft, and the intellectual system for the position - or if you will, the school - of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah: from the hadith scholars and Qur'an reciters, the Sufis of conduct and uprightness, the moderate Hanbalis, and others from the followers of the four schools that prevailed in the Sunni milieu and were accepted by the ummah in the practical jurisprudential field. He came to complete the building of this position - or the Sunni school - from the creedal side, in support of the rulings of the Book and the Sunnah, which had been disturbed by the tendencies of Mu'tazilism, extremism, dissension from the community, and Shi'ism, despite the efforts of Imam Abu Hanifah al-Nu'man (150 AH), the author of al-Fiqh al-Akbar and Risalah al-'Alim wa al-Muta'allim and others, such that some researchers consider him the founder of 'ilm al-kalam, but his efforts remained influential in the Hanafi field especially, and what al-Shafi'i and Ahmad - may Allah be pleased with them - did in resisting the innovators. And al-Ash'ari did that, because there became clear in his mind and settled in his heart during a long-term intellectual development - not as the symbolic stories imagine, from dream visions and seclusion for two or three weeks, then he emerges to people with new works and a consistent and integrated intellectual position, while he was a known thinker for years, rather decades, previously in the Mu'tazili milieu, associated with its greatest caller at that time, al-Jubba'i the elder, Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahhab - we say: there became clear in his mind and settled in his consciousness, in the middle of the last decade of the third century AH, when he was approaching forty, two matters: The first matter: approval of engaging in a new Sunni 'ilm al-kalam; so he issued a book with this title whose content matches his other book whose attribution to him is certain, which is: al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth, and the book al-Istihsan is nothing but a formulation
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological introduction discussing Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's role as an author and the intellectual context behind his work. It begins by affirming that al-Ash'ari was indeed an author and a writer, and that readers can perceive that he was laying the foundation of a new rational structure. This structure was not a personal or subjective school, but rather the rational formulation, theological craft, and intellectual system of the Sunni position, representing various groups: hadith scholars, Qur'an reciters, Sufis, moderate Hanbalis, and followers of the four legal schools. Al-Ash'ari came to complete the creedal aspect of this Sunni position in defense of the Qur'an and Sunnah against distortions from Mu'tazilism, extremism, sectarianism, and Shi'ism. The passage notes that earlier efforts by Abu Hanifah (considered by some the founder of kalam) were influential mainly in Hanafi circles, and that al-Shafi'i and Ahmad also fought innovators. Then it explains that al-Ash'ari's change was the result of a long intellectual development, not sudden dreams or retreats. He had been a known figure in the Mu'tazili school for decades, associated with al-Jubba'i. In his late thirties (around 290 AH), two matters became clear to him: first, the approval of engaging in a new Sunni kalam, leading him to write a book titled 'al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth' (Encouragement of Inquiry), and that the book 'al-Istihsan' is essentially a formulation of that encouragement.

Key Terms
علم الكلام
الاستحسان
الحث على البحث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari's turn to Sunni kalām was a sudden event triggered by dream visions or a short retreat.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that it was a long-term intellectual development, spanning years, not a brief episode.

Checkpoint
At what approximate age did al-Ash'ari realize the two matters according to the passage?
A) 30
B) 40
C) 50
D) 60

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's engagement with Sunni kalām was the result of a mature intellectual process, not a mystical conversion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief for years simply because it was the dominant view in your circle, like al-Ash'ari did with Mu'tazilism? Are you willing to re-examine your deepest convictions through long, honest study, even if it means leaving your comfort zone?
?
If your faith relies more on emotional experiences or dreams than on reasoned inquiry, how does al-Ash'ari's patient intellectual journey challenge you to seek a more grounded conviction?
?
Al-Ash'ari's two matters crystallized around age forty. What matters are crystallizing in your own heart and mind about your beliefs right now, and what are you doing to pursue them with the same depth and seriousness?
